كتاب الحدود الوطء الذي يوجب الحد ومحرمة نكحها ومَحْرَمة نكحها ) عطف على قوله : أجنبية ۱۹۱ [۱] قوله : ومحرمة نكحها ؛ عطف على قوله : «أجنبيّة» ؛ أي لا يحد من وطئ محرمة من محارمه كالأم والخالة والأخت ، بعدما نكحها، وهذه المسألة قد طعن بها جمع من الشيعة ومن يتشبه بهم من أهل السنة على أبي حنيفة وشهر بعضهم : إن وطء المحارم ونكاحهن حلال عند الحنفية. ومنهم من قال : إنّه خالف فيه الأحاديث الصحيحة، ولا عجب من الشيعة فإنهم قد طعنوا من غير مبالاة على أكبر من أبي حنيفة لله يعني الصحابة ، فما بالك بأبي حنيفة له ، إنّما العجب ممن تشبه بهم في اللعن والطعن، وسلك مسلكهم في الهمز واللمز، وهم من أهل السنّة ، بل عدّوا أنفسهم من متبعي الكتاب والسنة. فطعنوا على الإمام الهمام أبي حنيفة له في هذه المسألة طعناً تجاوز . وردوا عليه بأقبح الردّ من غير فهم مداركه والتأمل في دلائله. عنا الحد، وقد ألفت في هذه المسألة رسالة سمّيتها : «القول الجازم بسقوط الحد بنكاح المحارم»، شَيَّدت فيها مذهبه بالمعقول والمنقول، وأيدت فيها كلامه بالأصول، ودفعتُ تشكيكات المشككين على وجه يقصم ظهور المتعنتين، وذكرتُ ما يتعلق بها من الخلاف والفروع مع الجواب عن المطاعن والجروح، فإن شئت الاطلاع فارجع إليها، فإنّها نفيسة في بابها ، لا نظير لها في أبحاثها. ولنذكر نبذاً من المطاعن المشهورة فيما بين العوام مع الجواب عنها على ما يرتضيه الأعلام : فاعلم إنَّ من جملة مطاعنهم : 1. أن إسقاط الحد بوطء المحارم بعد نكاحهن مستلزم لحل هذا الفعل الشنيع ، وعدم لزوم إثم وملامة على مرتكب هذا القبيح، وهذا طعن باطل عند كل فاضل، فإن سقوط الحد أمر آخر، وحلّ الفعل أمر آخر، ولا يلزم من سقوط الحدّ في وطء حله، كيف فإنّ الحد يدرأ بالشبهات على ما ثبت ذلك بالأخبار والآثار الثابتة برواية الثقات ؛ ولذا حكم أبو حنيفة له أيضاً في واطئ المحارم بعد نكاحهن بأنه يعزر، ويوجعُ عقوبة، كما صرح به في «الهداية» وغيرها. (۱) «الهداية» (٥: ٢٥٩). (1) ومثلها قولهم : لَمَّا لم يجب الحد بوطء المحارم، دلّ ذلك على أنه لا يجب فيه شيء من العقوبة، وهذا قول باطل، فإنَّ الحد ليس عبارة عن كل جزاء عقوبة، بل هو عبارة عن عقوبة مقدرة تجب حقا الله ، فمعنى قولهم : يسقط الحد بوطء كذا وكذا إنه لا يجب عليه الجزاء المقدّر للزاني، وهو الرجم أو الجلد ؛ العروض شبهة أسقطته، لا أنه لا يجب شيء من العقوبة، ألا ترى إلى أنّ شرب الدم وأكل الخنزير ونحوهما من المحرمات مع كونها أشدّ من الزنى لا حدّ فيها مع وجوب التعزيز فيها. ٢. ومنها قولهم : إنّ أبا حنيفة خالف كتاب الله في هذه المسألة فإنّ الكتاب حكم بحرمة نكاح المحرمات، وحكم بوجوب الحدود على من زنى، وهو طعن مردود ؛ لأنّ أبا حنيفة لم يقل بحل وطئ المحارم أو بحل نكاحهن ، ولم يقل بعدم وجوب الحدّ على الزاني، حتى يكون مخالفاً لكتاب الله ، بل قال بسقوط حد الزني عن واطئ المحارم بعد نكاحهن ؛ لكون النكاح شبهة في الحلّ، والحدود تدرؤ بالشبهات»، بنص النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه ، ومع ذلك قال بوجوب التعزير حسبما يراه الإمام على ذلك المتمرد الخبيث الذي يطأ محارمه بعد النكاح. ٣. ومنها قولهم : إن أبا حنيفة لله خالف في هذا الباب الأحاديث الصريحة ، فأخرج الحاكم وصححه من حديث ابن عباس مرفوعاً: «من وقع على ذاتِ محرم فاقتلوه»، ومثله رواه الترمذي بسند ضعيف، وابن ماجة مع زيادة : «ومن وقع على بهيمة فاقتلوه واقتلوا البهيمة). وأخرج عبد الرزاق وابن أبي شَيْبَةَ والحاكم وصححه، والبيهقي عن البراء له قال : «لقيت خالي ومعه الراية ، فقلت : أين تريد ؟ فقال : بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى رجل صحيح الإسناد : (۱) في «المستدرك» (٤ : ٣٥٧) قال الحاكم : : هذا حديث ولم يخرجاه، و«جامع الترمذي (٤ : ٦٢) ، و (سنن ابن ماجه (۲) : (٨٥٦) ، و (مصنف عبد الرزاق(٧ : ٣٦٤) ، ومعتصر المختصر (۲) : ١٤١) ، و(مسند أحمد (۱ : ۳۰۰) ، و«المعجم الأوسط» (۹: ۱۳۸)، وغيرهم.
The Book of Hadd. Intercourse that necessitates hadd. "And a mahram he married" is an attachment to his statement: "an unrelated woman". Page 191. [1] His statement: "And a mahram he married" is an attachment to his statement: "an unrelated woman"; meaning, hadd is not applied to one who has intercourse with a mahram among his close relatives like the mother, maternal aunt, and sister, after he has married her. This matter has been attacked by a group of Shia and those who imitate them from the Ahl al-Sunnah against Abu Hanifa, and some of them have publicized that intercourse with mahrams and marrying them is permissible (halal) according to the Hanafis. And some of them said that he contradicted authentic hadiths in it. And there is no wonder from the Shia, for they have attacked without restraint those greater than Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with them, meaning the Companions, so what about Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him? Rather, the wonder is from those who imitate them in cursing and attacking, and follow their path in defamation and backbiting, while they are from the Ahl al-Sunnah; rather, they count themselves among the followers of the Book and the Sunnah. So they attacked the great Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, in this matter with an attack that exceeded [bounds], and they responded to him with the ugliest rejection without understanding his points and contemplating his evidences. Regarding hadd, I have composed a treatise on this matter which I named: "The Decisive Statement on the Falling of Hadd due to Marriage with Mahrams". In it, I strengthened his madhhab with rational and transmitted proofs, supported his statements with principles, and repelled the doubts of the doubters in a way that breaks the backs of the obstinate, and I mentioned the differences and branches related to it along with the response to the criticisms and defects. If you wish to examine it, then refer to it, for it is precious in its topic, with no equal in its investigations. We will mention a selection of the well-known criticisms among the common people along with the answers to them in a manner acceptable to the scholars. So know that among their criticisms are: 1. That the dropping of hadd for intercourse with mahrams after marrying them implies the permissibility of this vile act and the non-necessity of sin and blame on the perpetrator of this ugly deed. This is a false criticism according to every virtuous person, for the falling of hadd is one matter, and the permissibility of the act is another matter, and it does not follow from the falling of hadd for intercourse its permissibility. Why? Because hadd is averted by doubts (shubah) as established by reports and traditions transmitted by reliable narrators. Therefore, Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, also ruled concerning the one who has intercourse with mahrams after marrying them that he is to be given a discretionary punishment (yu'azzar) and is to receive a painful punishment, as stated in Al-Hidayah and other works. (1) Al-Hidayah (5:259). (1) And similar is their statement: "Since hadd is not obligatory for intercourse with mahrams, this indicates that no punishment whatsoever is obligatory for it." This is a false statement, for hadd is not every type of punishment; rather, it is a fixed punishment that is obligatory as a right of Allah. So the meaning of their statement "hadd falls for such-and-such intercourse" is that the fixed penalty for the fornicator, which is stoning or flogging, is not obligatory upon him due to a doubt that has caused it to fall; it is not that no punishment whatsoever is obligatory. Do you not see that drinking blood, eating pork, and similar prohibitions, despite being more severe than fornication, have no hadd, yet ta'zir is obligatory in them? 2. Among them is their statement: "Abu Hanifa contradicted the Book of Allah in this matter, for the Book ruled on the prohibition of marrying mahrams and ruled on the obligation of hudud on those who commit fornication." This is a rejected criticism, because Abu Hanifa did not say that intercourse with mahrams or marrying them is permissible, nor did he say that hadd is not obligatory on the fornicator, such that he would be contradicting the Book of Allah. Rather, he said that the hadd of fornication falls from the one who has intercourse with mahrams after marrying them due to the marriage being a doubt (shubha) regarding permissibility, and "hudud are averted by doubts" by the text of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and Companions. Nevertheless, he said that ta'zir is obligatory as deemed by the imam against that rebellious wicked person who has intercourse with his mahrams after marriage. 3. Among them is their statement: "Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, contradicted the explicit hadiths in this chapter." So al-Hakim recorded and deemed sahih from the hadith of Ibn Abbas marfu'an: "Whoever has intercourse with a mahram, kill him." Similarly, al-Tirmidhi narrated it with a weak chain, and Ibn Majah with an addition: "And whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill the animal." And Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Hakim (who deemed it sahih), and al-Bayhaqi recorded from al-Bara' who said: "I met my maternal uncle with the banner, and I said: 'Where are you going?' He said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, sent me to a man...' Sahih chain: (1) In Al-Mustadrak (4:357) al-Hakim said: "This hadith, and they did not record it," and Jami' al-Tirmidhi (4:62), and Sunan Ibn Majah (2:856), and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq (7:364), and Mukhtasar al-Mukhtasar (2:141), and Musnad Ahmad (1:300), and Al-Mu'jam al-Awsat (9:138), and others.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute defending the Hanafi position regarding the application of hadd (prescribed punishment) for intercourse with a mahram (close blood relative) after contracting a marriage with that relative. The author, writing in a later commentary, begins by affirming the ruling that hadd is not applied in such a case, citing the base text. He then addresses widespread criticisms from Shia and some lay Sunnis who claim that Abu Hanifa considered such acts permissible. The commentary systematically refutes three main objections.

First, the author clarifies that the fall of hadd does not imply permissibility (halal). Hadd is a fixed punishment that is averted by doubts (shubha) based on the established principle 'hudud are averted by doubts' (الحدود تدرأ بالشبهات). Abu Hanifa did not declare the act halal; rather, he ruled that the perpetrator receives a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) as stated in Al-Hidayah. Comparing this to other prohibitions like drinking blood or eating pork—which are more severe but carry no hadd—the author illustrates that the absence of hadd does not mean no punishment.

Second, the claim that Abu Hanifa contradicted the Quran is refuted. He never said the act is permissible; he only ruled that the specific hadd penalty for zina (adultery) does not apply because the marriage contract creates a doubt (shubha) that averts the fixed punishment. He did not deny the prohibition or the principle of hadd for zina, but found the hadd inapplicable due to the shubha. Ta'zir remains obligatory.

Third, the author addresses the charge of contradicting authentic hadiths that command killing a person who commits zina with a mahram. He notes that the hadiths cited are either weak, not taken as evidence, or not applicable because of the shubha. The chain of one hadith from Ibn Abbas is discussed, but the author implicitly argues that the hadith is either not sahih or overridden by the stronger principle of averting hadd through shubha. The passage ends with a list of sources where these hadiths are found.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that Abu Hanifa's position is based on solid hadith evidence (principle of shubha) and not on any claim of permissibility. The practical difference is that under Hanafi law, such a person is not executed or lashed with the hadd penalty but is subject to ta'zir (discretionary punishment) as determined by the judge.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or uncertainty that arises from a valid legal cause (such as a marriage contract) and prevents the application of hadd punishment.
تعزير (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment applied by the judge for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or kaffara; it is less than the fixed punishment and varies according to the circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the fixed punishment (hadd) not applied to a person who has intercourse with a mahram after marrying her?
A) Because the person has a valid marriage contract.
B) Because the act is considered halal.
C) Because of the doubt (shubha) created by the marriage contract.
D) Because the Quran does not explicitly forbid it.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is averted by shubha even for haram acts; the act remains prohibited and subject to ta'zir.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
advanced
12 min
Shubha and the Dropping of Hadd: Marrying a Mahram
Explains the ruling on intercourse with mahram after invalid marriage and the shubha that drops hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's position on hadd for intercourse with a mahram after an invalid marriage, the role of shubha in dropping the hadd, and the opposing view of the Sahibayn and three imams.

Core Idea
Even a weak shubha from an invalid marriage drops the hadd of zina; the principle 'Avert the hadd by shubhat' applies to all doubts.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a critical question in hudud: does a person who marries a mahram (like his father's wife) and has intercourse incur the hadd of zina? Abu Hanifa argues that the marriage contract, though invalid, creates a shubha that drops the hadd. The Sahibayn and the other three imams disagree, holding that hadd applies if the person knew the prohibition. We will examine the reasoning and the key evidence from the hadith and the precedent of 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
State exactly what is being disputed: whether the hadd of zina applies to a person who marries a mahram and has intercourse with her.
The act itself is haram by consensus; the dispute is about the penalty.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that the hadd is dropped due to shubha from the marriage contract, even if weak. His evidence includes the hadith 'Avert the hadd penalties by shubhat' and the precedent of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab who dropped the hadd for marriage during 'iddah.
The shubha exists because the contract resembles a valid marriage.
3
State the opposing position (Sahibayn and three imams)
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the three imams (Malik, Shafi‘i, Ahmad) impose the hadd if the person knows the prohibition. They argue that the contract is absolutely invalid (males) and cannot create any legal effect, so no shubha exists.
Knowledge of prohibition is essential for them.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to objections
The text responds to objections: shubha does not require the act to be permissible; it only requires a resemblance. The principle 'Avert the hadd' does not distinguish between strong and weak shubha. The lack of 'iddah or lineage does not negate the hadd-dropping effect.
Hadd is dropped by minimal doubt; other effects require stronger permissibility.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the person is not stoned or flogged for zina; the imam may administer ta‘zir at his discretion. Under the Sahibayn, the person receives the full hadd if knowledge is proven.
This difference has significant implications for enforcement.

كتاب الحدود الوطء الذي يوجب الحد
تزوج امرأة أبيه من بعده فأمرني أن أضرب عنقه وآخذ ماله، ومثله أخرجه الطحاوي وأبو داود وغيرهما.
والجواب عنه : إن القتل أو ضرب العنق أو أخذ المال المذكور في هذه الروايات ليس حداً للزني، يدلّ عليه أنها تدل بعمومها وإطلاقها على وجوب قتل كل من وقع على محرم، مع أن الرجم مختص بالمحصن إجماعاً.
اتفاقاً.
وأيضاً ورد في بعض الروايات القتل بتزوج ذات محرم، مع أن التزوج ليس بزنى
وأيضاً ورد في بعضها الأمر بأخذ المال، وهو ليس جزاء للزنى اتفاقاً. وأيضاً حد الزنى إنما هو الرجم والجلد مع التغريب أو بدونه اتفاقاً، والقتل المأمور به في هذه الأحاديث هو غير الجلد، وهو ظاهر، وغير الرجم، لا يكون بضرب العنق وقطع الرأس. وبالجملة : فهذا الذي أمره النبي الله إنما هو تعزيز وسياسة، وهذا مما لا ينكره أبو حنيفة له ، إنّما يقولُ بسقوط حدّ الزنى عمَّن نكح بمحرم ووطئه إلا بعدم وجوب تعزير عليه، بل يجب عنده على الإمامِ أن يقيم على مثل هذا الخبيث تعزيراً حسبما يراه على حسب تمردّه بأخذ المال، أو ضرب العنق ، أو نحو ذلك. فإن قلت : الوطء بالمحارم بدونِ النكاح موجب للحدّ اتفاقاً ، فكيف لا يو يوجبه بعد النكاح، وهو شناعة أخرى.
قلت : هذا ليس بمستبعد عند أرباب النقل والعقل، فإنّ الوطء بدون النكاح لا شبهة فيه، والنكاح يورث شبهة.
فإن قلت : النكاح بالمحارم فاسد قطعاً، فكيف يورث شبهة.
قلت : لا استبعاد في ذلك ؛ فإنّ الشبهة عبارة عَمّا يشبه الثابت وليس بثابت.
فإن قلت : هذه شبهة ركيكة.
(۱) في (صحيح ابن حبان (۹) : (٤۲۳) ، وجامع الترمذي (۳) : (٦٤٣) ، و(سنن الدارقطني (٣: ١٩٦)، و«المجتبى (٦ : (۱۰۹)، وسنن ابن ماجه (۲) : (٨٦٩) ، ومصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (۳) ٤٩٨)، وشرح معاني الآثار (۳) : (١٤٨) ، و(مسند البزار (٩ : ٢٥٥).
وهذا عند أبي حنيفة قلت : هب، ولكن حديث : «ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات)، لم يفرق بين شبهة وشبهة، فشبهة كونها منكوحة كافٍ وإن كانت ضعيفة، ونظيره ما روى مالك والشافعي وغيرهما : «إنّ عمر بن الخطاب له ضرب الذي نكح امرأة في عدتها من طلاق زوجها الأول، وضربها أيضاً وفرّق بينهما» (٢) ، مع أن النكاح في العدة حرام بنص الكتاب، وفاسد شرعاً ، لكن لما أورث ذلك شبهةً أسقط عمر بن الخطاب له عنهما حد الزني، وضربهما سياسة.
فان قلت : لو كانت الشبهة بالعقدِ ثابتةً لوجبت العدة وثبت النسب في نكاح المحارم.
قلت : منع بعض أصحابنا عدم وجوب العدة، وعدم ثبوت النسب، بناء على أن العقد يورث شبهة في حل المحل، وفي شبهة المحلّ يثبت النسب كما ذكره العيني وغيره، ولو سلم عدم وجوب العدة وعدم ثبوتِ النَّسب كما هو رأي بعض المشايخ ، نقول : مبنى وجوب العدّة وثبوتِ النسب على ثبوتِ حلّ المحل، ولو من وجه، وهاهنا لا حل للمحل ؛ أي المحارم أصلاً، والمراد بالحلّ أن يكون الواطئ على حال لا يلام بالوطء.
وأما سقوط الحد فهو لمجرد عروض شبهة بوجود ما يحلّل الوطء، وهو النكاحُ الموضوع الحل الاستمتاع، ولو كانت شبهةً ركيكة ، وبهذا يعلم أن الحد يسقط بالنكاح مطلقاً، وإن قال : علمت أنه حرام، صرح به في «الهداية». [1 قوله : عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ وبه قال سفيان الثوري، كما أخرجه الطحاوي في «شرح معاني الآثار»، وعندهما وعند الأئمة الثلاثة : يحدّ الواطئ بالمحارم بعد النكاح إذا كان عالماً بالحرمة ؛ لأنه عقد لم يصادف محلّه، فيلغو كما إذا أضيف إلى الذكور.
The book of hudud. The intercourse that necessitates the hadd. He married his father's wife after him, so he [the Prophet] ordered me to strike his neck and take his wealth. Similar was reported by al-Tahawi, Abu Dawud, and others. The response to it: The killing or striking the neck or taking the wealth mentioned in these reports is not a hadd for zina; this is indicated by the fact that they generally and absolutely indicate the obligation of killing everyone who commits intercourse with a mahram, while stoning is specific to the muhsan by consensus. Also, killing was reported in some reports regarding marrying a mahram, while marriage is not zina. Also, taking wealth was reported in some, which is not a punishment for zina by consensus. Also, the hadd for zina is only stoning and flogging with or without exile by consensus, and the killing commanded in these ahadith is other than flogging, which is apparent, and other than stoning, which is not by striking the neck and beheading. In summary: What the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded is only ta'zir and policy, and Abu Hanifa does not deny this. He only says that the hadd of zina is dropped from one who marries a mahram and has intercourse, except that ta'zir is not obligatory on him; rather, in his view, it is obligatory for the imam to administer ta'zir on such an evil person according to his discretion based on his defiance, by taking wealth, or striking the neck, or similar. If you say: Intercourse with mahrams without marriage necessitates the hadd by consensus, so why does it not necessitate it after marriage, which is another abomination? I say: This is not improbable for people of transmission and reason, for intercourse without marriage has no shubha, while marriage bequeaths shubha. If you say: Marriage to mahrams is absolutely invalid, so how does it bequeath shubha? I say: There is no improbability in that; for shubha is what resembles what is established while not being established. If you say: This is a weak shubha. [Footnote] And this is in the view of Abu Hanifa. I say: So be it, but the hadith 'Avert the hadd penalties by shubhat' did not differentiate between one shubha and another, so the shubha of being a wife suffices even if weak. Its parallel is what Malik, al-Shafi'i, and others reported: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) struck the one who married a woman during her 'iddah from the divorce of her first husband, and struck her as well, and separated them' while marriage during 'iddah is forbidden by the text of the Book and invalid legally, but because it bequeathed shubha, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab dropped the hadd of zina from them and struck them as policy. If you say: If the shubha by the contract were established, then 'iddah would be obligatory and lineage would be established in the marriage of mahrams. I say: Some of our companions deny the obligation of 'iddah and the establishment of lineage, based on the fact that the contract bequeaths shubha in the permissibility of the place, and in the shubha of the place, lineage is established as mentioned by al-'Ayni and others. And even if we concede the non-obligation of 'iddah and non-establishment of lineage as is the view of some mashayikh, we say: The basis of the obligation of 'iddah and establishment of lineage is the establishment of permissibility of the place, even from one aspect, and here there is no permissibility of the place at all, i.e., mahrams absolutely, and the intended meaning of permissibility is that the one having intercourse is in a state where he is not blameworthy for the intercourse. As for the dropping of the hadd, it is merely due to the occurrence of a shubha by the existence of something that makes the intercourse permissible, i.e., marriage, which is instituted for the permissibility of enjoyment, even if it is a weak shubha. And by this it is known that the hadd is dropped by marriage absolutely, even if he says he knew it was haram; this is stated in al-Hidayah. [Footnote text: His statement 'according to Abu Hanifa' – and Sufyan al-Thawri also held this view, as reported by al-Tahawi in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to the three imams: The one who has intercourse with mahrams after marriage is to be hadd if he knows the prohibition, because it is a contract that did not meet its proper place, so it is null, as if it were directed to males.]
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Hanafi ruling on whether a person who marries a mahram (a close relative, such as his father's wife) and then has intercourse with her incurs the hadd punishment for zina. The text begins by addressing a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the killing and confiscation of property of a man who married his father's wife. The author explains that this punishment is not the hadd of zina but rather ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and siyasa (policy). Abu Hanifa agrees with this but goes further: he holds that the hadd of zina is completely dropped due to the shubha (doubt) created by the marriage contract, even though the marriage itself is invalid. The text then presents a series of objections and responses. The first objection: intercourse with mahrams without marriage incurs hadd by consensus, so why not after marriage? The response: marriage introduces a shubha, while without marriage there is no shubha. The second objection: the marriage is absolutely invalid, so how can it create shubha? The response: shubha is defined as something that resembles what is true but is not actually true; the contract is a semblance of a valid marriage. The third objection: this shubha is very weak. The response: the principle 'Avert the hadd penalties by shubhat' does not differentiate between strong and weak shubha; even a weak shubha suffices. The example of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab is cited, who dropped the hadd of zina for a couple who married during 'iddah (waiting period), even though such marriage is forbidden and invalid. The text then addresses a possible inconsistency: if the shubha were effective, why does the marriage of mahrams not necessitate 'iddah and establish lineage? The author explains that some Hanafi scholars do hold that 'iddah is obligatory and lineage is established due to the shubha, but even if we accept the majority view that they are not, the dropping of hadd is separate — it is based on a minimal shubha that removes punishment, while 'iddah and lineage require a greater degree of permissibility of the place. Finally, the footnote clarifies that this is Abu Hanifa's view, shared by Sufyan al-Thawri, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold that the hadd is imposed if the person knew the marriage was prohibited, because the contract is null and cannot create any effect.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or resemblance to a permissible act that prevents the application of a hadd penalty; specifically the semblance of legality created by a marriage contract even if invalid.
محارم (mahārim): Close blood relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as mother, daughter, sister, etc.
تعزيز (ta'zīr): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion for crimes that do not have a fixed hadd, or for which hadd is dropped due to shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the hadd of zina dropped for a person who marries a mahram and has intercourse?
A) Because the marriage is valid and the act is halal
B) Because the marriage contract creates a shubha, even though the marriage is invalid
C) Because the person did not know the prohibition
D) Because the hadd is only for unmarried people

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, even a weak shubha from an invalid marriage suffices to drop the hadd of zina, based on the principle 'Avert the hadd by shubhat'.

Hadd for Intercourse with Mahram After Marriage: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether marriage with mahram creates shubha averting hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa drops the hadd for intercourse with a mahram after a marriage contract and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A marriage contract with a mahram creates a weak shubha that averts hadd according to Abu Hanifa, but Sahibayn require actual permissibility.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the limits of shubha (legal doubt). The core question: does an invalid marriage contract with a mahram create enough doubt to avert the hadd penalty? Abu Hanifa says yes, based on the hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts' and a rational argument about the contract's purpose. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree, and their view eventually becomes the relied-upon fatwa. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of shubha in hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules: the hadd is dropped because the marriage contract creates a shubha, even if weak, and even if the person knows the prohibition.
This is based on the general principle 'Duru al-hudud bi al-shubuhat'.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
Identify the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: hadd is applied if the person knows the prohibition, because the contract is void and does not create a valid shubha.
This view is also held by the three other imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad).
3
Analyze the basis of the dispute
Examine the key point of contention: whether the contract meets its mahall (place). Abu Hanifa says the mahall is capacity for procreation, which exists; Sahibayn say the mahall must accept permissibility (hull), which mahrams never do.
This distinction determines whether a shubha is created.
4
Evaluate the arguments
Consider Abu Hanifa's evidence: the hadith, Umar's precedent, and rational argument. Then consider the Sahibayn's rebuttal that the contract is void and no shubha arises.
The disagreement hinges on the definition of mahall.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Understand why later scholars (Abu al-Layth, al-Khulasa) preferred the Sahibayn's view: true shubha requires some aspect of permissibility, which is absent.
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's position.

Source Text

وهذا عند أبي حنيفة قلت : هب، ولكن حديث : «ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات)، لم يفرق بين شبهة وشبهة، فشبهة كونها منكوحة كافٍ وإن كانت ضعيفة، ونظيره ما روى مالك والشافعي وغيرهما : «إنّ عمر بن الخطاب له ضرب الذي نكح امرأة في عدتها من طلاق زوجها الأول، وضربها أيضاً وفرّق بينهما» (٢) ، مع أن النكاح في العدة حرام بنص الكتاب، وفاسد شرعاً ، لكن لما أورث ذلك شبهةً أسقط عمر بن الخطاب له عنهما حد الزني، وضربهما سياسة. فان قلت : لو كانت الشبهة بالعقدِ ثابتةً لوجبت العدة وثبت النسب في نكاح المحارم. قلت : منع بعض أصحابنا عدم وجوب العدة، وعدم ثبوت النسب، بناء على أن العقد يورث شبهة في حل المحل، وفي شبهة المحلّ يثبت النسب كما ذكره العيني وغيره، ولو سلم عدم وجوب العدة وعدم ثبوتِ النَّسب كما هو رأي بعض المشايخ ، نقول : مبنى وجوب العدّة وثبوتِ النسب على ثبوتِ حلّ المحل، ولو من وجه، وهاهنا لا حل للمحل ؛ أي المحارم أصلاً، والمراد بالحلّ أن يكون الواطئ على حال لا يلام بالوطء. وأما سقوط الحد فهو لمجرد عروض شبهة بوجود ما يحلّل الوطء، وهو النكاحُ الموضوع الحل الاستمتاع، ولو كانت شبهةً ركيكة ، وبهذا يعلم أن الحد يسقط بالنكاح مطلقاً، وإن قال : علمت أنه حرام، صرح به في «الهداية». [1 قوله : عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ وبه قال سفيان الثوري، كما أخرجه الطحاوي في «شرح معاني الآثار»، وعندهما وعند الأئمة الثلاثة : يحدّ الواطئ بالمحارم بعد النكاح إذا كان عالماً بالحرمة ؛ لأنه عقد لم يصادف محلّه، فيلغو كما إذا أضيف إلى الذكور. فإنه جعل النكاح شبهة في درء الحد وله : إنّ العقد صادف محلّه ؛ لأنّ محلَّ التصرف ما يقبلُ مقصوده، والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد، وهو المقصود ، فكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في حق جميع الأحكام إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحلّ، فيورث الشبهة ؛ لأنّ الشبهة ما يشبه الثابت، وليس بثابت ، كذا في «الهداية». وفي «البحر» أخذاً من «فتح القدير» (۲) : حاصلُ الخلاف أنّ هذا العقد هل يوجبُ شبهة أم لا ؟ ومداره على أنه هل وردّ على محلّه أم لا ، فعند الإمام الله ورد على ما هو محله ؛ لأنّ المحليّة ليست بقبول الحل، بل بقبول المقاصد من العقد، وهو ثابت ؛ ولذا صح من غيره العقد عليها. وعندهما : لا ؛ لأنّ محل العقد ما يقبلُ حكمه ، وهو الحل، وهذه من المحرمات في سائر الأحوال، فكان الثابت صورة العقدِ لا انعقاده، وقد أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث بقولهما، وقال في «الواقعات»: ونحن نأخذ به أيضاً، وفي «الخلاصة»: الفتوى على قولهما، ووجه ترجيحه أن تحقق الشبهة يقتضي تحقق الحلّ من وجه ؛ لأنّ الشبهة لا محالة شبهة المحلّ، لكن حلّها ليس بثابت من وجه. انتهى ملخصاً.
And this is according to Abu Hanifa. I said: Granted, but the hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts' does not differentiate between one doubt and another. So the doubt that she is a married woman is sufficient even if weak. Its parallel is what Malik and al-Shafi'i and others narrated: 'Indeed Umar ibn al-Khattab, may God be pleased with him, beat the one who married a woman during her idda from the divorce of her first husband, and also beat her and separated them,' although marriage during the idda is forbidden by the text of the Book and invalid legally, but because that created a doubt, Umar ibn al-Khattab dropped the hadd of zina from them, and beat them as a policy. If you say: If the doubt by the contract were established, then the idda would be obligatory and lineage would be established in the marriage of mahrams. I say: Some of our companions denied the obligation of idda and the establishment of lineage, on the basis that the contract creates a doubt regarding the permissibility of the place (mahall), and in doubt of the place, lineage is established as al-Ayni and others mentioned. And even if we concede that idda is not obligatory and lineage is not established, as is the view of some mashayikh, we say: The basis for the obligation of idda and establishment of lineage is the establishment of the permissibility of the place, even from one aspect, and here there is no permissibility of the place at all, i.e., mahrams absolutely. And what is meant by permissibility is that the one who has intercourse is not blameworthy for intercourse. As for the dropping of the hadd, it is merely due to the occurrence of a doubt through the existence of something that makes intercourse permissible, which is marriage, which is established for the permissibility of enjoyment, even if the doubt is weak. And by this it is known that the hadd is dropped by marriage absolutely, even if he says 'I knew it was forbidden.' It is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah. [1 His statement: according to Abu Hanifa; and Sufyan al-Thawri also said this, as recorded by al-Tahawi in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to the three Imams, the one who has intercourse with mahrams after marriage is to be hadded if he knows the prohibition, because it is a contract that did not meet its place (mahall), so it is void, as if it were added to males. For he made marriage a doubt in warding off the hadd. And his proof: The contract met its place because the place of a transaction is what accepts its intended purpose, and the female of the daughters of Adam is capable of procreation, which is the intended purpose. So it should have been valid with respect to all rulings, except that it fell short of effectively conferring true permissibility, thus it creates a doubt. For the doubt is that which resembles what is established but is not established. So it is in al-Hidayah. And in al-Bahr, taken from Fath al-Qadir: The summary of the disagreement is whether this contract creates a doubt or not. And the hinge is on whether it was directed at its place or not. According to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), it was directed at its place because being a place (mahalliyya) is not by accepting permissibility, but by accepting the purposes of the contract, and that is established; hence it is valid from others to contract upon her. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): No, because the place of a contract is what accepts its ruling, which is permissibility, and these (mahrams) are forbidden in all circumstances, so what is established is the form of the contract, not its validity. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted their view, and he said in al-Waqi'at: And we also adopt it. And in al-Khulasa: The fatwa is on their view, and the reason for its preference is that the verification of doubt necessitates the verification of permissibility in some aspect, because doubt is inevitably doubt about the place, but its permissibility is not established in any aspect. End of summary.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary (sharh) on the Hidayah, dealing with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a marriage contract with a mahram (an unmarriageable kin) creates sufficient legal doubt (shubha) to avert the hadd penalty for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse). The author first presents Abu Hanifa's position: the hadd is dropped because of the shubha arising from the contract, citing the hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts' and the precedent of Umar ibn al-Khattab who, despite the clear prohibition of marriage during idda, dropped the hadd due to the doubt and only administered a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The author then addresses an objection: if the contract creates doubt, why does it not also establish idda and lineage? The response is that idda and lineage require actual permissibility (hull) of the intercourse, which does not exist here because the woman is perpetually forbidden (mahram). However, the hadd is dropped simply because there is a doubt that the intercourse might have been permissible, even if weak. The text then clarifies the disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa, the contract did meet its place (mahall) because the mahall of a marriage contract is a woman capable of bearing children, and that capability exists; thus the contract is valid in principle but falls short of actual permissibility, creating a doubt. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the contract is void because its mahall must accept the ruling (hukm) of the contract, which is permissibility, and a mahram never accepts permissibility. Therefore, no shubha is created and hadd applies if the person knew the prohibition. Later scholars like Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi and the author of al-Khulasa preferred the Sahibayn's view, and the fatwa is on their position. The text ends with a summary from al-Bahr and Fath al-Qadir. The passage is rich in legal reasoning, distinguishing between the purposes of a contract and its effective validity, and the nature of shubha.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Legal doubt or ambiguity that arises from an external factor (here, a marriage contract with a mahram) making an unlawful act resemble a lawful one, even if weak.
محارم (mahārim): Unmarriageable kin (e.g., mother, sister, daughter) with whom marriage is permanently forbidden.
حد (ḥadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by the Quran and Sunnah for certain crimes (here, zina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) No hadd is applied because the marriage contract creates a shubha.
B) Hadd is applied if he knew the prohibition.
C) Only ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is given.
D) The marriage is valid and no punishment is needed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that a marriage contract with a mahram does not create sufficient shubha to avert hadd if the person knew the prohibition, because shubha requires some aspect of permissibility.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shubha from Void Marriage Preventing Hadd
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shubha from void marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether a void marriage creates shubha to avert hadd, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A void marriage's shubha depends on whether the mahall accepts the contract's objective or its ruling.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: does a marriage contract that is void (like marrying a mahram) create a legal doubt (shubha) sufficient to avert the hadd punishment for zina? The answer hinges on how we define the 'place' (mahall) of the contract. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, the reasoning behind each, and which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Recognize that the core question is whether a void marriage creates shubha to prevent hadd. Note that the debate is within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa vs. the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa defines the mahall of a marriage contract as any human female capable of procreation. Since the contract encounters such a mahall, it should have full effect but falls short of permissibility, thus creating shubha. This applies to all void marriages regardless of the type of prohibition.
Key concept: 'mahall is what accepts the objectives of the contract, not the ruling.'
3
Examine the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that the mahall must accept the ruling (permissibility) of the contract. For eternally prohibited women (e.g., mahrams), the mahall never accepts permissibility, so only the form of the contract is established, not its legal conclusion. Hence no shubha. They distinguish between disputed marriages (like without witnesses) and universally prohibited ones.
Key concept: 'mahall is what accepts the ruling of the contract.'
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, hadd is never imposed for any void marriage if the person knew it was haram. Under the Sahibayn, hadd is not imposed for disputed marriages (e.g., without witnesses) if the person admits prohibition, but is imposed for universally prohibited marriages (e.g., sister) if he admits prohibition.
This difference has real-world implications for hudud cases.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position and its basis
Later scholars like Abu al-Layth and the author of Al-Khulasa preferred the Sahibayn's view. The tarjih reason: genuine shubha requires permissibility from some aspect, which is absent in eternally prohibited unions. The fatwa is given accordingly.
Know the authority weight: from Zahir al-Riwayah but tarjih by later mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنه جعل النكاح شبهة في درء الحد
وله : إنّ العقد صادف محلّه ؛ لأنّ محلَّ التصرف ما يقبلُ مقصوده، والأنثى من بنات آدم قابلة للتوالد، وهو المقصود ، فكان ينبغي أن ينعقد في حق جميع الأحكام إلا أنه تقاعد عن إفادة حقيقة الحلّ، فيورث الشبهة ؛ لأنّ الشبهة ما يشبه الثابت، وليس بثابت ، كذا في «الهداية»(۱).
وفي «البحر» أخذاً من «فتح القدير» (۲) : حاصلُ الخلاف أنّ هذا العقد هل يوجبُ شبهة أم لا ؟ ومداره على أنه هل وردّ على محلّه أم لا ، فعند الإمام ورد على ما هو محله ؛ لأنّ المحليّة ليست بقبول الحل، بل بقبول المقاصد من العقد، وهو ثابت ؛ ولذا صح من غيره العقد عليها. وعندهما : لا ؛ لأنّ محل العقد ما يقبلُ حكمه ، وهو الحل، وهذه من المحرمات في سائر الأحوال، فكان الثابت صورة العقدِ لا انعقاده، وقد أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث بقولهما، وقال في «الواقعات»: ونحن نأخذ به أيضاً، وفي «الخلاصة»: الفتوى على قولهما، ووجه ترجيحه أن تحقق الشبهة يقتضي تحقق الحلّ من وجه ؛ لأنّ الشبهة لا محالة شبهة المحلّ، لكن حلّها ليس بثابت من وجه. انتهى ملخصاً(۳).
(1) قوله : فإنه جعل النكاح شبهة ؛ أي مطلقاً ، فلا يحد بالوطء بعد تزوج محارمه، وكذا تزوج منكوحة الغير، ومعتدته، ومطلقة الثلاث، وكذا نكاحُ الخامسة في عدة الرابعة ونكاحُ أختِ الزوجة في عدتها، ونكاح المجوسية، والأمة على الحرة ، ونكاح العبد أو الأمة بلا إذن المولى، والنكاح بغير شهود ففي كل هذا لا يجب الحد عنده ، وإن قال : علمت أنه حرام. وعندهما : لا يحد وإن قال : إنّه حرام في كلِّ نكاح مختلف في صحته وفساده، كالنكاح بغير شهود، والنكاح بغير ولي، ونكاح المتعة والمؤقت، وأما النكاح المتفق على حرمته فلا يسقط الحدّ عندهما إذا أقر بالحرمة.
وقيل : قولهما بعدم سقوط الحدّ عند الإقرار بالحرمة ليس مطلقاً، بل في نكاح امرأة محرمة على التأبيد، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إلى «القول الجازم» وفيما ذكرناه هنا كفاية للعالم الفاهم.
He made marriage a shubha in averting the hadd. And for him: The contract encountered its place because the place of transaction is what accepts its objective, and the female of the children of Adam is capable of procreation, which is the objective. So it should have been concluded with respect to all rulings except that it fell short of conferring the reality of permissibility, thus it creates shubha; because shubha is what resembles the established but is not established. Thus in Al-Hidayah. And in Al-Bahr, taken from Fath al-Qadir: The essence of the dispute is whether this contract entails shubha or not. Its basis is whether it occurred in its place or not. According to Imam [Abu Hanifa], it occurred in its place because 'placeness' is not by acceptance of permissibility but by acceptance of the objectives of the contract, and that is established; hence it is valid from others to contract upon her. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]: No, because the place of the contract is what accepts its ruling, which is permissibility, and she is among the eternally prohibited women. So what is established is the form of the contract, not its conclusion. Faqih Abu al-Layth took their view and said in Al-Waqi'at: We also take it. And in Al-Khulasa: The fatwa is on their view. The reason for its preference is that the realization of shubha necessitates realization of permissibility from one aspect, because shubha is inevitably a shubha of the place, but its permissibility is not established from an aspect. End summarized. (1) His saying: He made marriage a shubha; i.e., absolutely, so one is not hadded for intercourse after marrying his mahrams, and likewise marrying another's wife, her waiting period, the triple-divorced woman, and likewise marrying a fifth woman during the waiting period of the fourth, marrying the sister of the wife during her waiting period, marrying a Zoroastrian woman, a slave woman over a free woman, a slave or slave girl without the master's permission, marriage without witnesses — in all of these, hadd is not obligatory according to him, even if he says: I knew it is forbidden. According to the two, he is not hadded if he says it is forbidden in every marriage that is disputed in its validity and invalidity, like marriage without witnesses, marriage without a guardian, mut'ah and temporary marriage. As for marriage universally agreed upon its prohibition, the hadd is not dropped according to them if he admits the prohibition. It is said: Their view of not dropping the hadd upon admission of prohibition is not absolute, but rather in the marriage of an eternally prohibited woman. If you wish further detail, refer to Al-Qawl al-Jazim. What we have mentioned here is sufficient for the knowledgeable person.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a void but contractually valid marriage (nikah fasid) creates a legal shubha (doubt) sufficient to avert the hadd punishment for zina. The text begins by citing Al-Hidayah that marriage itself is considered a shubha in averting hadd. The reasoning: a contract encountering its proper place (mahall) — a human female capable of procreation, which is the objective — should have full effect, but it falls short of conferring actual permissibility (halal), hence creates a shubha (resemblance of the established). The essence of the dispute is whether such a contract occurs on its proper place. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'placeness' is defined by capacity to receive the contract's objectives (procreation), not by the resulting permissibility. Since the woman is capable, the contract occurs on its place, thus creating shubha. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the place of a contract must accept its ruling (permissibility). Since the woman is eternally prohibited (e.g., a mahram), she never accepts the ruling of halal, so only the form of the contract is established, not its legal conclusion, hence no shubha. Later Hanafi scholars like Abu al-Layth and the author of Al-Waqi'at adopted the Sahibayn's view. The fatwa in Al-Khulasa is on their view, with the reasoning that genuine shubha requires permissibility from some aspect, which is absent here. The footnote elaborates that according to Abu Hanifa, hadd is not imposed in all cases of disputed marriage even if the person acknowledges the prohibition, while the Sahibayn differentiate: if the marriage is disputed (e.g., without witnesses), hadd is not imposed upon admission of prohibition; but if the marriage is universally agreed to be prohibited (e.g., with a mahram), hadd is not dropped if he admits the prohibition. Some say the Sahibayn's view applies only to eternally prohibited women.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt or resemblance to a valid right; specifically, a situation that resembles a valid marriage but is not actually valid, sufficient to avert the hadd punishment for zina.
محل العقد (mahall al-'aqd): The place or subject of the contract; in marriage, the woman being married. The condition of the mahall determines the contract's effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, in which of the following cases is the hadd for zina not imposed even if the person admits the prohibition?
A) A man marries his sister, knowing it is haram.
B) A man marries a woman during her iddah from another, knowing it is haram.
C) A man marries a woman without witnesses, knowing it is haram.
D) A man marries a woman universally agreed to be mahram, knowing it is haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the effect of a void marriage on hadd depends on whether the prohibition is disputed or universal; the mufta bihi (Sahibayn's view) imposes hadd for universally prohibited marriages if the person admits prohibition.

No Hadd for Bestiality and Sodomy: Ta'zir Only
States no hadd for bestiality and sodomy; ta'zir required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and sodomy, explain why they do not incur hadd, and identify the evidence and its interpretation.

Core Idea
Bestiality and sodomy are not zina; they require discretionary punishment (ta'zir), not the fixed penalty of hadd.

This lesson examines the legal distinction between zina and other prohibited sexual acts. The Hanafi school, as articulated in the passage, restricts the fixed punishment of hadd to vaginal intercourse between unmarried parties. Bestiality and sodomy fall outside this definition and are therefore subject to ta'zir, a discretionary punishment determined by the judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the two acts discussed: bestiality and sodomy (liwat). Note that the passage explicitly states there is no hadd for either.
The text says 'لا حد' (no hadd).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited. For bestiality: 'مَن أتى البهيمة فاقتلوه واقتلوا البهيمة معه'. For sodomy: 'من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به'.
Both orders to kill are found in Sunan compilations.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the Hanafis interpret the imperative 'اقتلوا' (kill). They do not take it as a fixed hadd because the acts are not zina; rather, the command indicates a severe ta'zir at the imam's discretion.
The ruling could be overridden by istihsan if a lighter punishment serves the public interest better.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider sodomy as zina deserving hadd. Hanafis differentiate based on the linguistic and legal definition of zina.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the imam must impose ta'zir, which can include severe punishment like death if necessary, but no fixed hadd.
The text confirms 'نعم يجب عليه التعذير البليغ' (yes, a severe ta'zir is obligatory).

والحكمة في قتل البهيمة قطع التحدث بفعل الواطئ.
(٢) قوله : أو أتى ؛ عطف على قوله : مَن وطئ ؛ أي لا يُحدّ من عَمِلَ عمل قوم سيدنا لوط على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام، وهو أن يأتي دُبُرَ المرأة أو الرجل، نعم يجب عليه التعذير البليغ يدلّ عليه قوله : «من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به ، أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة وأحمد وعبد الرزاق وابن أبي الدنيا والدارقطني والبيهقي والحاكم وصححه.
وأخرج ابن أبي شَيْبَة وابن أبي الدنيا والبيهقي عن ابن عباس له أنه سئل : «ما حد اللواطة ؟ قال : ينظر أعلى بناء بالقرية فيلقي منه منكساً، ثم يتبع بالحجارة»، وأخرج الواقدي في «كتاب الردة» : «إنَّ أبا بكر الصديق له أمر بإحراقه بالنار».
Or a beast, or one who comes in the rectum. (Or a beast, or one who comes in the rectum): This is according to Abu Hanifa upon its prohibition, so the hadd does not fall according to the two if he admits the prohibition. It is said: Their view of not dropping the hadd upon admission of prohibition is not absolute, but rather in the marriage of an eternally prohibited woman. If you wish further detail, refer to Al-Qawl al-Jazim. What we have mentioned here is sufficient for the knowledgeable person. [1] His saying: 'or a beast' is conjoined to 'a foreign woman'; i.e., there is no hadd on one who sexually assaults an animal like a sheep, cow, and the like, because it is not zina, neither linguistically nor legally, nor is it in its meaning in causing corruption of the bed and loss of offspring. Yes, the imam must give him a ta'zir that reforms him. This is indicated by his statement: 'Whoever has sex with a beast, kill him and kill the beast with him' — narrated by the four Sunan compilations and others. The wisdom in killing the beast is to cut off talk about the act of the assailant. (2) His saying: 'or one who comes' is conjoined to his saying: 'whoever has intercourse'; i.e., one who does the act of the people of our master Lot (peace be upon him) — which is to come in the rectum of a woman or a man — is not hadded. Yes, a severe ta'zir is obligatory upon him, as indicated by his statement: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lot, kill the doer and the one with whom it is done' — narrated by the four Sunan, Ahmad, Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, al-Darqutni, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Hakim, who authenticated it. And Ibn Abi Shayba, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn Abbas that he was asked: 'What is the hadd for sodomy?' He said: 'Look at the highest building in the village, throw him off it upside down, then pelt him with stones.' And al-Waqidi narrated in Kitab al-Riddah that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq ordered him to be burned with fire.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and sodomy (liwat). According to Abu Hanifa, these acts do not incur the hadd punishment prescribed for zina because they are not zina linguistically or legally. Zina is specifically defined as penile-vaginal intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other. Bestiality lacks the element of human partnership, and sodomy (anal intercourse, whether with a woman or a man) is a different act. The text explains that bestiality does not cause confusion of lineage (nasab) or loss of offspring, which are the primary harmful consequences of zina. Instead, the imam must administer a ta'zir (discretionary punishment) that is suitable and reformative. The author cites a hadith from the Sunan collections ordering the killing of both the perpetrator and the animal, but Hanafis interpret this not as a fixed hadd but as a severe ta'zir that can include execution in extreme cases, though the preferred view is ta'zir without death. For sodomy, the hadith 'kill the doer and the one with whom it is done' is similarly understood by Hanafis as a recommendation for severe ta'zir, not a mandatory hadd. The passage also reports companion practice: Ibn Abbas recommended throwing the offender from a height and stoning, and Abu Bakr ordered burning, indicating that extreme punishments were permitted as ta'zir, not hadd. The key point: no hadd is fixed for these acts, but the state may impose severe discretionary punishment.

Key Terms
بهيمة (bahima): A non-human animal (beast); in this context, any animal with which one commits bestiality.
لواطة (liwatah): Sodomy; the act of the people of Lot, i.e., anal intercourse, whether with a woman or a man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Hadd of stoning to death
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment) imposed by the imam
D) No punishment because it is not a crime

Key Takeaway
Bestiality and sodomy are not zina and therefore do not trigger fixed hadd punishments; they require discretionary ta'zir.

Bestiality: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir
Commentary on bestiality ruling from Al-Wiqayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and explain why it incurs ta'zir rather than hadd.

Core Idea
Bestiality is not zina; thus no hadd, only discretionary ta'zir.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies the Hanafi position on intercourse with animals. The author distinguishes bestiality from zina, both linguistically and legally, and explains that the fixed punishment (hadd) for zina does not apply. Instead, a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) is prescribed, backed by a hadith that is interpreted as a policy punishment rather than a fixed hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Hanafi Ruling
The act is intercourse with an animal (bahīmah). The Hanafi ruling is that there is no fixed hadd punishment; instead, the Imam must administer ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
2
Understand Why It Is Not Zina
The passage states that bestiality is not zina linguistically or legally, and does not share the underlying rationales (corruption of lineage, loss of offspring) that justify the severe fixed penalty of zina.
This reasoning excludes analogy (qiyas) to zina.
3
Note the Punishment: Ta'zir, Not Hadd
The text emphasizes that the Imam must give a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) suitable to the offender. This is not a fixed penalty but is determined by the judge based on the circumstances.
Ta'zir may include beating, imprisonment, or other deterrent measures.
4
Analyse the Proof (Hadith) and Its Interpretation
The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill the animal with him.' Although the command 'kill him' appears absolute, it is interpreted as ta'zir, not a fixed hadd, because it lacks conditions of hadd (e.g., no distinction between muhsan and non-muhsan).
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut, further supporting its interpretation as a policy punishment.
5
Consider the Wisdom (Hikmah)
The animal is killed to cut off talk about the act and to remove the object of temptation. This is a discretionary measure, not a fixed punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١]قوله : أو بهيمة ؛ عطف على أجنبية ؛ أي لا حدَّ على من وطء حيواناً كالشاةِ والبقر ونحوهما ؛ لأنه ليس بزني، لا لغة ولا شرعاً، ولا هو في معناه في كونه باعثاً لفساد الفراش وضياع الولد، نعم يجب على الإمام له أن يعزّره تعزيراً يصلح له، ويدل عليه قوله ل ل الله : مَن أتى البهيمة فاقتلوه واقتلوا البهيمة معه»(۱) ، أخرجه أصحابُ السنن الأربعة وغيرهم. والحكمة في قتل البهيمة قطع التحدث بفعل الواطئ.
[1] His statement: 'or an animal' is conjuncted to 'a foreign woman'; meaning there is no fixed punishment (hadd) on one who has intercourse with an animal like a sheep, cow, and the like, because it is not zina, neither linguistically nor legally, nor is it in its meaning regarding causing corruption of the bed and loss of offspring. Yes, it is obligatory upon the Imam to give him a disciplinary punishment (ta'zir) suitable for him. And it is indicated by his statement (صلى الله عليه وسلم): 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill the animal with him,' reported by the authors of the four Sunan and others. And the wisdom in killing the animal is to cut off talk about the act of the perpetrator.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, explaining the ruling on bestiality. The author first clarifies that the phrase 'or an animal' in the matn is conjuncted to 'a foreign woman', meaning that just as there is no hadd for intercourse with a foreign woman under certain conditions (as previously discussed), there is no hadd for intercourse with an animal. The reason is that bestiality is not zina, either linguistically or legally, and it does not share the underlying rationales of zina such as causing corruption of lineage and wasting offspring. Therefore, the prescribed punishment (hadd) for zina does not apply. Instead, the Imam must administer a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) appropriate to the offender. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم): 'Whoever has intercourse with an animal, kill him and kill the animal with him.' This hadith, though it mentions killing, is interpreted as a discretionary punishment, not a fixed hadd. The wisdom in killing the animal is to prevent people from talking about the act and to remove the object of temptation.

Key Terms
بهيمة (bahīmah): An animal, specifically a quadruped like sheep, cow, etc.
تعزير (taʿzīr): A discretionary punishment determined by the imam, not fixed in shari'ah.
حد (ḥadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by shari'ah for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Bestiality is not zina in Hanafi fiqh; therefore, it incurs only ta'zir, not a fixed hadd punishment.

Hadd or Ta'zir for Liwat? The Hanafi Position and Its Critics
Intra- and inter-madhhab dispute on liwat punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liwat and evaluate the opposing arguments from the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i regarding the application of the hadd punishment.

Core Idea
Anal intercourse does not incur the fixed hadd of zina according to Abu Hanifa, only severe ta'zir; the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i argue for the hadd.

This passage examines a key intra- and inter-madhhab dispute: does sodomy (liwāṭah) carry the same fixed punishment as fornication (zinā)? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, holds that it does not, while the two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) and Imam al-Shāfiʿī argue that it does based on analogy and textual implication. This lesson unpacks the evidence and objections, revealing the methodological principles behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core dispute
The act is liwat (anal intercourse). The dispute is whether it incurs the hadd of zina or only ta'zir.
The Hanafi school defines liwat as a separate offence from zina.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) and its evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that there is no hadd; only ta'zir. Evidence: the hadith commanding killing both parties is interpreted as policy (siyasa), not a fixed hadd, because it does not distinguish between muhsan and non-muhsan.
The lack of distinction indicates it is not the hadd of zina, which distinguishes the two.
3
State the opposing position (Sahibayn / al-Shafi'i) and its evidence
They hold that liwat incurs the hadd of zina. Evidence: liwat shares the same effective cause (illa) as zina—fulfilling desire in a prohibited and desired place, wasting seed, and perpetual prohibition. They derive this by implication of the text (dalālat al-nass) on zina, not by pure qiyas.
They also cite reports of stoning from Companions.
4
Analyse the objections raised against the opposing position
Two objections are raised: (1) the meaning derived from the text (dalālat al-nass) must be linguistically self-evident, which it is not; (2) the true rationale of zina includes destruction of lineage and confusion of lineage, which are absent in liwat.
The passage cuts off before the complete Hanafi response, but these objections show the methodological differences.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, punishment is discretionary (ta'zir), allowing the judge to decide severity. Under the Sahibayn/al-Shafi'i, it is a fixed hadd: stoning for muhsan and 100 lashes for non-muhsan, but only when the act is with strangers (not with one's slave or wife).
This difference affects the legal process and the possibility of pardon or mitigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢) قوله : أو أتى ؛ عطف على قوله : مَن وطئ ؛ أي لا يُحدّ من عَمِلَ عمل قوم سيدنا لوط على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام، وهو أن يأتي دُبُرَ المرأة أو الرجل، نعم يجب عليه التعزير البليغ يدلّ عليه قوله : «من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به» ، أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة وأحمد وعبد الرزاق وابن أبي الدنيا والدارقطني والبيهقي والحاكم وصححه. وأخرج ابن أبي شَيْبَة وابن أبي الدنيا والبيهقي عن ابن عباس له أنه سئل : «ما حد اللواطة ؟ قال : ينظر أعلى بناء بالقرية فيلقي منه منكساً، ثم يتبع بالحجارة»، وأخرج الواقدي في «كتاب الردة» : «إنَّ أبا بكر الصديق له أمر بإحراقه بالنار». أما عندهما وعند الشَّافِعِي (١) له في أحد قوليه يحد حد الزنا ؛ لأنه في معنى الزنا. [١]قوله : أما عندهما ... الخ ؛ روى نحوه عن علي له : «نه» رجم لوطيّاً ) (۲) ، أخرجه ابن أبي شَيْبَة، وابن أبي الدنيا والبيهقي، ومثله روى عندهم عن الحسن البصري وإبراهيم النخعي ، ويشهد له من المرفوع حديث ابن ماجة والحاكم بلفظ : «مَن عَمِلَ عمل قوم لوط فارجموا الفاعل والمفعول به»(۳). وهو عند أبي حنيفة له محمول على السياسة بدليل عدم الفصل بين المحصن وبين غير المحصن، ولو كان الإتيان الدبر زنى يوجب الفصل بينهما. ثم عندها : إنما يحدّ إذا فعل ذلك بالأجانب، فإن أُتي في دُبُرِ عبده أو أمته أو زوجته لم يحد بل يعزّر. (۲) قوله : لأنه في معنى الزنى ؛ أشار به إلى أن وجوب الحد عندهما في اللواطة بدلالة نص ورد في الزنى لا بالقياس ، فاندفع ما أورد عليهما أن الحدود لا تثبت بالقياس. وحاصل كلامهما : إن المعنى الذي يُفْهَمُ من نص ورد في الزنى : قضاء الشهوة بسفح الماء في محل محرّم ومشتهى وهذا موجود في اللواطة، بل زيادة؛ لأنها في الحرمة وسفح الماء فوقه، فإن حرمتها لا تزولُ أبداً ، وفيه تضييع الماء على وجه لا يخلق منه الولد، والإيراد عليه من وجوه : أحدها : إنّ المعتبر في دلالةِ النص هو كون المعنى الذي لأجله الحكم بحيث يفهمه كل من يعرفُ اللغة، وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك. وثانيها : إنا لا نُسلّم أنّ المعنى الذي لأجله وجبَ الحد في الزنى، هو ما ذكر، بل قضاء الشهوة في محل مشتهى محرّم ، مع هلاك البشر وإفساد الفراش واشتباه النسب، وهذا غير موجود في اللواطة، وموجود في الزنى، فإنّ فيه هلاك البشر ؛ لأن ولد الزنا هو
(2) His statement: 'or one who comes (to the anus)' is conjuncted to his statement: 'whoever has intercourse'; i.e., there is no fixed punishment for one who does the act of the people of our master Lut (peace be upon him), which is to come to the anus of a woman or a man. Yes, a severe discretionary punishment (ta'zir) is obligatory upon him, indicated by his statement: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lut, kill the active and passive partner.' Reported by the authors of the four Sunan, Ahmad, Abdurrazzaq, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Hakim who authenticated it. And Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, and al-Bayhaqi reported from Ibn Abbas that he was asked: 'What is the punishment for liwat?' He said: 'Look at the highest building in the town, throw him from it upside down, then pelt him with stones.' And al-Waqidi reported in 'Kitab al-Ridda': 'Abu Bakr al-Siddiq ordered him to be burnt with fire.' As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to al-Shafi'i in one of his two opinions, he is given the hadd punishment of zina because it is in the meaning of zina. [1] His statement: 'As for according to the two...' etc.; something similar is reported from Ali: 'He stoned a sodomite' – reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, and al-Bayhaqi, and similarly reported from al-Hasan al-Basri and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. And it is supported by the marfu' hadith of Ibn Majah and al-Hakim: 'Whoever does the act of the people of Lut, stone the active and passive partner.' But according to Abu Hanifa, this is interpreted as a matter of policy (siyasa), evidenced by the absence of distinction between muhsan and non-muhsan. If anal intercourse were zina, it would necessitate a distinction between them. Then according to them (the two): he is only given the hadd if he does it with foreigners (ajānib); if he comes to the anus of his slave, slave-girl, or wife, he is not given hadd but is given ta'zir. (2) His statement: 'because it is in the meaning of zina' – he indicated by this that the obligation of hadd according to the two in liwat is by implication of the text (dalālat al-nass) that came in zina, not by qiyas, thus rebutting the objection against them that hadd punishments are not established by qiyas. The gist of their statement: The meaning understood from the text that came in zina is: fulfilling desire by pouring water in a prohibited and desired place. And this is present in liwat, indeed more so, because in prohibition and pouring water it is even stronger, for its prohibition never ends, and it wastes water in a way that does not create offspring. And objections are raised against it from several aspects: First: What is considered in the implication of the text (dalālat al-nass) is that the meaning for which the ruling is established is such that anyone who knows the language understands it, and what we are dealing with is not like that. Second: We do not concede that the meaning for which the hadd is obligatory in zina is what was mentioned. Rather, (it is) fulfilling desire in a desired prohibited place along with destruction of humans, corruption of the bed, and confusion of lineage. And this is not present in liwat but present in zina, because in it there is destruction of humans: since the child of zina is...
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding liwat (sodomy). The author begins by stating the position of the matn (and Abu Hanifa): there is no fixed hadd punishment for liwat; rather, a severe discretionary punishment (ta'zir) is given. The proof is the hadith commanding the killing of both parties, which is interpreted as a policy punishment, not a fixed hadd, because there is no distinction between muhsan and non-muhsan in this hadith. Additional evidence from the actions of the Companions is cited. The passage then presents the disagreement of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i (in one of his two opinions): they hold that liwat incurs the hadd of zina because it is analogous to zina. They argue that the underlying rationale (illa) of zina – fulfilling desire in a prohibited and desired place, wasting seed, and the act being perpetually prohibited – is present in liwat, even more so. They derive this not by pure qiyas but by implication of the text (dalālat al-nass). The commentator then raises two objections against this reasoning: first, that the meaning derived from the text must be linguistically evident (which it is not); second, that the true rationale of zina includes the destruction of humanity (through illegitimate children) and confusion of lineage, which are absent in liwat. The text cuts off before providing the full Hanafi response.

Key Terms
لواطة (liwāṭah): Sodomy, i.e., anal intercourse (with a man or woman).
دبر (dubur): Anus; the site of the act in liwat.
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment, severe here.
سياسة (siyāsah): Policy; here referring to discretionary justice (al-siyasa al-shar'iyya).
دلالة النص (dalālat al-nass): Implication of the text; an inferential method where the ruling is extended based on a meaning understood from the text, even if not explicitly stated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best summarizes Abu Hanifa's argument against applying the hadd of zina to liwat?
A) Liwat is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) The hadith commanding killing does not distinguish between muhsan and non-muhsan, indicating it is policy, not a fixed hadd.
C) The Sahibayn's analogy is weak because liwat is less severe.
D) Ta'zir is always preferable to hadd.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, as established by Abu Hanifa, treats liwat as a separate offense from zina, punishable by ta'zir rather than a fixed hadd, though the Sahibayn and others disagree.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
