Dispute on Sodomy's Hadd Punishment
Dispute on whether sodomy incurs hadd punishment as zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sodomy's hadd, explain the proof from dalālat al-naṣṣ, and evaluate the five objections raised against it.

Core Idea
Sodomy is a major sin, but does it equal zina for hadd? The Hanafi school splits on this very question.

This lesson explores a sharp legal disagreement within the Hanafi school (and with al-Shafi‘i) on whether sodomy (lawāṭah) incurs the same fixed punishment (ḥadd) as fornication/adultery (zinā). The source passage presents the arguments of both sides, with the later Hanafi position (muftā bihī) leaning toward the ḥadd. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of textual indication (dalālat al-naṣṣ) and the structure of effective causes (‘ilal) in Ḥudūd.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi intra-school positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa (ta‘zīr only) versus that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (ḥadd of zinā for non-maḥram cases). Note that al-Shafi‘i has two opinions, one agreeing with each.
The difference is not on sinfulness – all agree it is a major sin – but on the legal penalty.
2
Analyze the proof of the Sahibayn
They rely on dalālat al-naṣṣ: the text prohibiting zinā implies that any act sharing its essential meaning (satisfying desire by depositing fluid in a prohibited, desired place) also incurs the ḥadd. They cite the hadith 'Kill the doer and the one upon whom it is done' as supporting evidence.
They claim this is not qiyās but direct indication from the text, thus avoiding the rule that ḥudūd are not established by analogy.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's objections
Abu Hanifa raises five objections: (1) the meaning is not self-evident to every Arabic speaker; (2) the ‘illa of zinā includes additional elements (destruction of lineage, corruption of bed, confusion of progeny) absent in sodomy; (3) wasting fluid is sometimes permissible (e.g., ‘azl); (4) desire in sodomy is one-sided, making it less prevalent; (5) deficiency in parts of the ‘illa prevents establishing the ruling (cf. urine vs. wine).
Objections 2 and 5 are the most substantive from an uṣūl perspective.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa prescribes ta‘zīr (discretionary punishment) for all cases of sodomy. The Sahibayn prescribe ḥadd (stoning or lashing) if the act is with a non-maḥram; if with a wife or own slave, ta‘zīr only.
The muftā bihī in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn: ḥadd applies.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
Al-Marghinānī in al-Hidāyah and later Ḥanafīs prefer the Sahibayn’s view. The authority_weight is ẓāhir al-riwāyah, and the ruling is considered muftā bihī.
Thus, the operative fatwā in the Hanafi school is that sodomy with a non-maḥram incurs the ḥadd of zinā.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود / الوطء الذي يوجب الحد
أما عندهما وعند الشَّافِعِي له في أحد قوليه يحد حد الزنا ؛ لأنه في معنى الزنا
قوله : أما عندهما ... الخ ؛ روى نحوه عن علي له : «نه» رجم لوطيّاً ) ، أخرجه ابن أبي شَيْبَة، وابن أبي الدنيا والبيهقي، ومثله روى عندهم عن الحسن البصري وإبراهيم النخعي ، ويشهد له من المرفوع حديث ابن ماجة والحاكم بلفظ : «مَن عَمِلَ عمل قوم لوط فارجموا الفاعل والمفعول به».
وهو عند أبي حنيفة له محمول على السياسة بدليل عدم الفصل بين المحصن وبين غير المحصن، ولو كان الإتيان الدبر زنى يوجب الفصل بينهما. ثم عندها : إنما يحدّ إذا فعل ذلك بالأجانب، فإن أُتي في دُبُرِ عبده أو أمته أو زوجته لم يحد بل يعزّر.
قوله : لأنه في معنى الزنى ؛ أشار به إلى أن وجوب الحد عندهما في اللواطة بدلالة نص ورد في الزنى لا بالقياس ، فاندفع ما أورد عليهما أن الحدود لا تثبت بالقياس.
وحاصل كلامهما : إن المعنى الذي يُفْهَمُ من نص ورد في الزنى : قضاء الشهوة بسفح الماء في محل محرّم ومشتهى وهذا موجود في اللواطة، بل زيادة؛ لأنها في الحرمة وسفح الماء فوقه، فإن حرمتها لا تزولُ أبداً ، وفيه تضييع الماء على وجه لا يخلق منه الولد، والإيراد عليه من وجوه :
أحدها : إنّ المعتبر في دلالةِ النص هو كون المعنى الذي لأجله الحكم بحيث يفهمه كل من يعرفُ اللغة، وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك. وثانيها : إنا لا نُسلّم أنّ المعنى الذي لأجله وجبَ الحد في الزنى، هو ما ذكر، بل قضاء الشهوة في محل مشتهى محرّم ، مع هلاك البشر وإفساد الفراش واشتباه النسب، وهذا غير موجود في اللواطة، وموجود في الزنى، فإنّ فيه هلاك البشر ؛ لأن ولد الزنا هالك حكماً، وفيه إفساد الفراش ؛ أي فراش الزوج. وثالثها : إن تضييع الماء قاصر في الحرمة ، فلا يوجب الحد ألا ترى أنه قد يحل بالعزل.
ورابعها : إنّ الشهوة في الزنى من الطرفين لميلان طبعهما إليه، بخلاف اللواطة، فإن الشهوة فيها من جانب الفاعل فقط، والمفعولُ يمتنع عنها بطبعه، على ما هو مقتضى الجبلة السليمة، فيكون الزنى أغلب وجوداً وأسرع حصولاً، فيكون إلى الزاجر أحوج.
وخامسها : إنّ حرمة اللواطة وإن كانت أشدّ من حرمة الزني ؛ ولذا لا تحل أبداً ، لكنها لا تنفع في إيجاب الحدّ ؛ لأنّ زيادة بعض أجزاء علّة الحكم في شيء مع نقصان في البعض، كالشهوة وسفح البعض، وانتفاء البعض كهلاكِ البشر وإفساد الفراش، واشتباه النَّسب لا يوجب ثبوت الحكم فيه، ألا ترى إلى أنّ شرب البول فوق شرب الخمر في الحرمة، مع أنه لا يوجب الحد، هذا توضيح ما في «التنقيح» وشرحه «التوضيح»، وحاشية «التلويح»
قوله : تمحض حراماً ؛ فقد وردت أحاديث كثيرة بحرمة إتيان الدبر ، كحديث : «اقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به» على ما مر ذكره. وحديث : «إنّ الذي يأتي في دُبُرها - أي المرأة - لا ينظر الله إليه يوم القيامة» أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجة وأحمد وابن أبي شَيْبَة والبيهقي وغيرهم.
Book of Hudud / Intercourse that necessitates hadd... As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to al-Shafi'i in one of his two opinions: he is punished with the hadd of zina; because it is in the meaning of zina. His statement: 'As for according to them... etc.'; a similar narration is reported from Ali: 'He stoned a sodomite' – recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Abi al-Dunya, and al-Bayhaqi. Similarly, it is reported from al-Hasan al-Basri and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Supporting it from marfu' hadith is the narration of Ibn Majah and al-Hakim with the wording: 'Whoever does the deed of the people of Lot, execute the doer and the one upon whom it is done.' And according to Abu Hanifa, it is interpreted as a discretionary punishment (siyasah), evidenced by the lack of distinction between the muhsan and non-muhsan; if anal intercourse were zina, it would necessitate such a distinction. Then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): He is only punished with hadd if he does it with a non-mahram; if he penetrates the anus of his slave, slave-girl, or wife, he is not punished with hadd but is given ta'zir. His statement: 'because it is in the meaning of zina'; he indicated by this that the obligation of hadd for sodomy according to them is by the indication (dalalah) of a text concerning zina, not by qiyas, so the objection that hudud are not established by qiyas is refuted. The gist of their argument: The meaning understood from the text concerning zina is: satisfying desire by the pouring of fluid in a prohibited and desired place, and this exists in sodomy, even more so; because its prohibition is permanent, and the pouring of fluid is above that, for its prohibition never ceases, and it involves wasting fluid in a manner that no child is created from it. Objections to it from several aspects: First: The consideration in the indication of the text (dalalah al-nass) is that the meaning for which the ruling exists is such that every speaker of the language understands it, and this is not the case here. Second: We do not concede that the meaning for which the hadd is obliged in zina is what they mentioned; rather it is satisfying desire in a desired prohibited place, along with destruction of human life, corruption of bed (lineage), and confusion of lineage. This is not present in sodomy, but is present in zina; for in zina there is destruction of human life because the child of zina is considered destroyed; and corruption of the husband's bed. Third: The wasting of fluid is limited in prohibition, so it does not necessitate hadd; do you not see that it is permitted by 'azl (coitus interruptus)? Fourth: Desire in zina is from both sides due to natural inclination, unlike sodomy where desire is only from the active partner, and the passive partner naturally avoids it, according to sound nature; thus zina is more prevalent and quicker, so it is more in need of a deterrent. Fifth: Although the prohibition of sodomy is stronger than that of zina – thus it is never permissible – this does not help in necessitating hadd; because increase of some parts of the cause of a ruling in something along with deficiency in other parts – such as desire and pouring of fluid partially present, and absence of others like destruction of human life, corruption of bed, and confusion of lineage – does not necessitate the establishment of the ruling. Do you not see that drinking urine is stronger in prohibition than drinking wine, yet it does not necessitate hadd? This is the clarification of what is in al-Tanqih and its commentary al-Tawdih, and the gloss al-Talwih. His statement: 'it is purely prohibited'; indeed many hadiths have been reported on the prohibition of anal intercourse, such as the hadith: 'Kill the doer and the one upon whom it is done' as mentioned earlier, and the hadith: 'The one who penetrates her anus – i.e., a woman – Allah will not look at him on the Day of Resurrection' recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ahmad, Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi, and others.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether the act of sodomy (lawatah) incurs the same hadd punishment as zina (fornication/adultery). The author presents the position of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), and al-Shafi'i (in one of his two opinions): that sodomy does incur the hadd of zina because it shares the same core meaning (ma'na) – satisfying sexual desire by depositing fluid in a prohibited and desired place. They support this with hadith narrations, including a marfu' hadith: 'Whoever does the deed of the people of Lot, execute the doer and the one upon whom it is done.' However, they specify that this hadd applies only with a non-mahram; if the act is done with one's slave, slave-girl, or wife, the punishment is ta'zir (discretionary) not hadd.

In contrast, Abu Hanifa holds that sodomy is not zina and does not warrant the hadd punishment. His evidence is that the Companions differed on its punishment, including burning or walling in, which indicates it is not equivalent to zina. Moreover, he observes that if it were zina, there would be a distinction between the muhsan (married) and non-muhsan offender – the muhsan would be stoned and the non-muhsan lashed – but the Sahibayn do not make this distinction; they apply the same hadd regardless. Thus, Abu Hanifa interprets the hadith about execution as a matter of state policy (siyasah), not a fixed hadd.

The passage then details the Sahibayn's argument that the hadd is established by the indication of the text (dalalah al-nass) concerning zina, not by qiyas, thereby avoiding the objection that hudud cannot be analogized. They claim that the effective cause ('illa) – fulfilling desire by depositing fluid in a prohibited, desired place – is present in sodomy even more intensely.

The Hanafi commentator refutes this with five objections: (1) The meaning derived from the text must be self-evident to any Arabic speaker, which this is not. (2) The true 'illa of hadd in zina includes additional elements: destruction of human life (the illegitimate child), corruption of marriage bed, and confusion of lineage – none of which exist in sodomy. (3) The 'wasting of fluid' is not a strong enough cause for hadd, since it can be permissible by 'azl. (4) Desire in zina is mutual, whereas in sodomy only the active partner desires it; thus zina is more widespread and needs a stronger deterrent. (5) Even though sodomy is more severely prohibited, the deficiency in the other parts of the 'illa prevents the imposition of hadd, just as drinking urine is more prohibited than wine but does not incur hadd.

The dispute thus turns on whether sodomy shares the full effective cause of zina. For Abu Hanifa, it does not, so the punishment is ta'zir, not hadd.

Key Terms
اللواطة (al-lawāṭah): Sodomy, specifically anal intercourse between males or with a woman per anum
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): Indication from the explicit wording of a text that conveys a ruling through understood meaning, not through qiyas
معنى (ma‘nā): The effective cause or ratio legis understood from the text, used here to analogize sodomy to zina

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what punishment does a man incur for committing sodomy with his wife?
A) Hadd of zina (stoning or lashes)
B) Ta'zir only
C) No punishment because it is permissible
D) Execution based on the hadith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that sodomy with a non-mahram incurs the hadd of zina, based on dalālat al-naṣṣ, despite Abu Hanifa's own view of ta'zir only.

Sodomy Does Not Incur Hadd: Hanafi Rational Proofs
Ruling with multiple rational proofs that sodomy is not zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sodomy (liwata) and explain why it does not incur hadd, using the five rational proofs presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Sodomy is more prohibited than zina but does not incur hadd because the causes of hadd are absent.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya defends the Hanafi position that sodomy (liwata) is not zina and thus does not require the fixed punishment of hadd. The author presents five rational arguments, building on the Companions' disagreement, to show that despite its severe prohibition, sodomy lacks the effective causes (mutual desire, destruction of lineage) that trigger hadd. The final analogy to drinking urine being more prohibited than wine yet incurring no hadd crystallizes the principle: the severity of prohibition does not automatically impose a hadd penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Locate the opening statement: 'it is not fornication' (ليس بزنا). This is the core ruling being proven.
The passage builds on the fact that the Companions differed on the punishment.
2
List the five rational proofs (adillah aqliyyah)
Go through each numbered proof: (1) lack of natural desire from both sides, (2) no destruction of lineage or marital bed corruption, (3) 'wasting water' is less severe, analogous to coitus interruptus, (4) one-sided desire makes it less frequent so less need for deterrent, (5) increased prohibition does not entail hadd because essential elements (cause of hadd) are absent.
Each proof aims to show that the 'illa (effective cause) for hadd is missing in sodomy.
3
Analyze the analogy (tamthil) of drinking urine
Notice the final argument: urine is more prohibited than wine but no hadd. This illustrates that severity of sin does not automatically require hadd; the specific cause (intoxication for wine) is absent. Similarly, the cause for hadd in zina (mutual desire, lineage confusion) is absent in sodomy.
This is a qiyas of a higher order (qiyas al-shabah) comparing the absence of the 'illa.
4
Confirm the Hanafi ruling and note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is that sodomy incurs ta'zeer, not hadd. The Shafi'i school equates sodomy with zina and applies hadd. Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The passage is a defense of the Hanafi view against opponents (implicitly Shafi'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله أنه ليس بزنا، فإنَّ الصَّحابة اختلفوا في موجبه : من الإحراق، وهدم الجدار هالك حكماً، وفيه إفساد الفراش أي فراش الزوج. وثالثها : إن تضييع الماء قاصر في الحرمة ، فلا يوجب الحد ألا ترى أنه قد يحل بالعزل. ورابعها : إنّ الشهوة في الزنى من الطرفين لميلان طبعهما إليه، بخلاف اللواطة، فإن الشهوة فيها من جانب الفاعل فقط، والمفعولُ يمتنع عنها بطبعه، على ما هو مقتضى الجبلة السليمة، فيكون الزنى أغلب وجوداً وأسرع حصولاً، فيكون إلى الزاجر أحوج. وخامسها : إنّ حرمة اللواطة وإن كانت أشدّ من حرمة الزني ؛ ولذا لا تحل أبداً ، لكنها لا تنفع في إيجاب الحدّ ; لأنّ زيادة بعض أجزاء علّة الحكم في شيء مع نقصان في البعض، كالشهوة وسفح البعض، وانتفاء البعض كهلاكِ البشر وإفساد الفراش، واشتباه النَّسب لا يوجب ثبوت الحكم فيه، ألا ترى إلى أنّ شرب البول فوق شرب الخمر في الحرمة، مع أنه لا يوجب الحد، هذا توضيح ما في «التنقيح» وشرحه «التوضيح»، وحاشية «التلويح»
And for him (Abu Hanifa) it is not fornication. The Companions differed regarding its punishment: burning, demolishing a wall, treating as lost legally, and corrupting the bed (i.e., the husband’s bed). Third: wasting water is less severe in prohibition, so it does not necessitate the hadd; do you not see that it may be permissible with coitus interruptus. Fourth: desire in fornication is from both sides due to natural inclination, unlike sodomy, where desire is only from the doer and the passive partner abstains by nature, as per sound constitution; so fornication is more frequent and quicker in occurrence, thus more in need of a deterrent. Fifth: the prohibition of sodomy is more severe than that of fornication, hence it is never permissible, but this does not cause the hadd because an increase in some parts of the cause of a ruling with a decrease in others, like desire and emission, and the absence of others like destruction of progeny and corruption of bed and confusion of lineage, does not necessitate establishing the ruling; do you not see that drinking urine is more prohibited than drinking wine, yet it does not necessitate the hadd. This is the clarification from al-Tanqih, its commentary al-Tawdih, and the gloss al-Talwih.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining why sodomy (liwata) is not considered zina and therefore does not incur the hadd (fixed corporal punishment) according to the Hanafi school. The author presents five rational arguments (dalil 'aqli) building on the fact that the Companions differed on the punishment. First, sodomy does not involve full satisfaction in the natural place of desire. Second, it does not destroy lineage or corrupt the marital bed fundamentally. Third, wasting sperm by sodomy is less severe in prohibition than in zina, as it can be permissible by 'azl (coitus interruptus). Fourth, desire in sodomy is one-sided, unlike zina where both parties naturally desire, making sodomy less prevalent and thus less needing a harsh deterrent. Fifth, even though sodomy is more severely prohibited, the purpose of the hadd is to protect lineage, progeny, and marital bed—elements absent in sodomy—so it is analogous to drinking urine: more prohibited but no hadd. The Hanafi position is that the offender is given ta'zeer (discretionary punishment), which may include imprisonment, beating, or even death if he habituates (siyasatan), but not the fixed hadd.

Key Terms
اللواطة (al-liwatah): Sodomy, anal intercourse between men or with a woman.
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes.
التعزير (al-ta'zeer): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it lacks the effective cause of hadd: destruction of lineage and mutual desire.

D) Because the hadd for sodomy is burning, which is not a fixed hadd.

Key Takeaway
Sodomy, though more severely prohibited than zina, does not incur hadd because the effective causes (mutual desire, lineage protection) are absent.

Zina in Dar al-Harb or Dar al-Baghy: Hadd Suspended
Inter-madhhab dispute on hadd for zina outside Islamic territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for zina in enemy territory, explain the key proof (Zayd ibn Thabit), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hadd for zina requires deterrence; without Imam's authority, obligation is fruitless.

This passage addresses a key territorial limitation on hudud punishments. While zina is a major sin, its hadd (fixed punishment) is not automatically applied everywhere. The Hanafi school argues that the purpose of hadd is deterrence, which requires the Imam's enforcement authority. In territories where that authority is absent—Dar al-Harb (non-Muslim enemy territory) and Dar al-Baghy (rebel territory)—the obligation of hadd is suspended. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules: no hadd for zina committed in Dar al-Harb or Dar al-Baghy. Also note the additional clause about a non-mukallaf (insane/child) with a mukallaf.
The text says 'ولا بزنا غير مكلف بمكلفة أصلاً' – that is a separate but related ruling.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a Muslim's acceptance of Islam commits him to all rulings wherever he is; territorial boundaries do not exempt him from hadd.
This is a general principle in Shafi'i usul: Islamic law applies universally to Muslims.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the purpose (maqsad) of hadd is deterrence (inzijar). Deterrence requires the Imam's authority to execute the punishment. In Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Baghy, that authority is severed, so the obligation becomes fruitless (futile).
Also note that the act itself did not become a cause (sabab) for hadd while in that territory; it does not become so upon return.
4
Examine the transmitted proof (dalil naqli)
The Hanafi proof includes the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit: 'Hadds are not established in Dar al-Harb for fear that he may join its people.' This shows a Companion-derived precedent.
This is a qawl al-sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: If a Muslim fornicates in a non-Muslim country and then returns to an Islamic state, the Hanafi judge will not apply hadd; the Shafi'i judge will. This has real implications for legal extradition and cross-border crimes.
The text also implies an exception: if the Muslim is part of an army with a commanding Imam, the hadd is applied because authority exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو زنى في دار الحرب أو بغي، ولا بزنا غير مكلف بمكلفة أصلاً. هذا عندنا خلافاً للشافعي. له : إنّه التزم بإسلامه جميع أحكامه أينما كان. ولنا : إن المقصود هو الإنزجار، وولاية الإمام الذي إليه إقامة الحدود منقطعة في دار الحرب ودار البغي فيخلو الوجوب عن الفائدة، ولما لم ينعقد فعله موجباً لم يجب عليه الحد بعدما خرج أيضاً، ويؤيده قول زيد بن ثابت : لا تقام الحدود في دار الحرب مخافة أن يلحق بأهلها.
Or if one commits fornication in the Abode of War or Abode of Rebellion, and there is no fornication between a non-accountable person and an accountable person at all. This is according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. For him (Shafi'i): He (the Muslim) by his Islam committed to all rulings wherever he is. And for us: The purpose is deterrence, and the authority of the Imam who administers the hadds is severed in Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Baghy, so the obligation becomes fruitless. And since his act did not become a cause (for hadd), he is not obligated to hadd afterwards either. And supporting this is the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit: 'The hadds are not established in Dar al-Harb for fear that he may join its people.'
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position: if a Muslim fornicates in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory) or Dar al-Baghy (rebel territory) and is not in a camp where the ruler's authority exists, then no hadd is imposed. This includes the case where a non-mukallaf (insane or child) fornicates with a mukallafa. The Shafi'i argues that once a person accepts Islam, all rulings, including hadd, apply wherever he is. The Hanafi response: the purpose of hadd is deterrence (inzijar), and the Imam's authority to administer hadd ends at the border of such territories; thus the obligation becomes meaningless. Moreover, the act itself is not effective as a cause for hadd while in that land, and it does not become so after returning. The Hanafi proof is the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit that hadds are not executed in Dar al-Harb. This ruling is specific to those who go out voluntarily or as traders; if a soldier is with a commander who has authority, the hadd is applied.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule with no treaty with Muslims; hostilities can occur.
دار البغي (Dar al-Baghy): Territory held by Muslim rebels against the legitimate Imam.
غير مكلف (ghayr mukallaf): Not legally accountable: a child, insane person, or one not meeting conditions of taklif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because zina is not a sin in Dar al-Harb.
B) Because the Imam's authority to implement hadd is severed there.
C) Because the offender is considered a non-Muslim.
D) Because the hadd would cause him to join the enemy.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the application of hadd for zina is contingent on the Imam's territorial authority; without it, the obligation of hadd is suspended.

No Hadd for Zina in Enemy Territory: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on hudud jurisdiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on hadd for zina in Dar al-Harb or Dar al-Baghy and contrast it with the Shafi'i view, including the dalil and thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
No hadd in enemy territory: jurisdiction is lost, deterrence is void.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya tackles a key inter-madhhab dispute: does a Muslim who commits zina in non-Muslim or rebel territory face the fixed punishment upon return? The Hanafi school, drawing on the purpose of hadd as deterrence and the limits of the Imam's authority, holds that the obligation is cancelled. Al-Shafi'i argues that embracing Islam entails universal application of rulings. Let's examine the proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school does not impose hadd for zina committed in Dar al-Harb or Dar al-Baghy.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the person remains in that territory or returns.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite view: the Muslim must accept all Islamic rulings wherever they are.
His basis is the universal commitment of Islam.
3
Follow the opponent's dalil
Al-Shafi'i argues that by embracing Islam, the person undertook all its rulings, so jurisdiction is universal.
No distinction between dar al-Islam and others.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with the purpose of hadd (deterrence) and the Imam's cut-off authority in those territories; the act does not become binding.
Supporting evidence: narration of Zayd ibn Thabit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Muslim returning from Dar al-Harb is not punished under Hanafi law but would be under Shafi'i.
This affects legal enforcement in Muslim states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو زنى في دار الحرب أو بغي (۱) ، هذا عندنا خلافاً للشَّافِعِي . [٣] قوله : خلافاً للشافعي له : له : إنّه التزم بإسلامه جميع أحكامه أينما كان. ولنا : إن المقصود هو الإنزجار ، وولاية الإمام الذي إليه إقامة الحدودِ منقطعة في دار الحرب ودار البغي فيخلو الوجوب عن الفائدة ، ولَما لم ينعقد فعله موجباً لم يجب عليه الحد بعدما خرج أيضاً، ويؤيده قول زيد بن ثابت له : «لا تقام الحدود في دار الحرب مخافة أن يلحق بأهلها ، أخرجه البيهقي.
Or he committed zina in Dar al-Harb or Dar al-Baghy. This is according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [3] His statement: contrary to al-Shafi'i: He said: He committed himself by his Islam to all its rulings wherever he is. And for us: The intended purpose is deterrence, and the authority of the Imam who establishes hudud is cut off in Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Baghy, so the obligation becomes fruitless. Since his act was not binding, the hadd is not obligatory upon him even after he exits. This is supported by the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit: 'Hudud are not established in Dar al-Harb for fear that he might join its people,' narrated by al-Bayhaqi.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states that if a Muslim commits zina in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory) or Dar al-Baghy (rebel territory), the hadd punishment is not applied according to the Hanafi school. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that since he is Muslim, all Islamic rulings apply wherever he is. The Hanafi response is that the purpose of hadd is deterrence (inzijar), but the Imam's jurisdiction to enforce it is absent there, so the obligation serves no purpose. Moreover, his act in enemy territory is not considered a fully consummated offense that would necessitate punishment upon return. This is supported by the narration of Zayd ibn Thabit that hudud are not established in enemy territory to prevent the person from joining them out of fear. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule, not bound by Islamic law.
دار البغي (Dar al-Baghy): Territory controlled by rebels against the legitimate Imam.
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for certain crimes (e.g., zina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the Imam's jurisdiction is cut off, rendering the obligation futile.

D) Because the hadd is only for Muslims within Islamic territory.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not impose hadd for zina committed in non-Muslim or rebel territory due to the absence of the Imam's jurisdiction and the loss of deterrent purpose.

No Hadd When One Party is Non-Mukallaf
Ruling with proof that no hadd applies to either party when one is not legally responsible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd when one party in zina is not legally responsible and explain the rationale based on legal capacity.

Core Idea
No hadd falls on either party when one is not legally responsible — legal capacity is the foundation of criminal liability.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: when a person lacking legal capacity (ghayr mukallaf) commits zina with a legally responsible person (mukallaf), no hadd is applied to either. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies this rule and cites a hadith as supporting evidence. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi principle that hadd penalties require both parties to be mukallaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Zina involving a non-mukallaf and a mukallaf. The hukm is that no hadd applies to either party.
The ruling is absolute: no hadd on the non-mukallaf and no hadd on the mukallaf.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith: 'ملعون من أتى امرأة في دبرها' (Cursed is the one who approaches a woman in her anus), narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ahmad.
The hadith is about anal intercourse, not zina in the usual sense, but it is used to support the general prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The hadith condemns the act but does not prescribe a hadd punishment. It serves as a deterrent, not a basis for a fixed penalty.
The commentary implies that such acts are cursed but not subject to hadd under the conditions.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih; some other schools may punish the mukallaf party, but Hanafis exempt both.
The disagreement stems from different views on whether hadd requires both parties to be mukallaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa), based on the principle that hadd requires full legal responsibility of both parties.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, giving it strong authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بزنا غير مكلف بمكلّفة أصلاً. (ولا بزنا غير مكلف بمكلّفة أصلاً) أي لا على هذا، ولا على هذه وحديث : «ملعون من أتى امرأة في دبرها (۳) ، أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وأحمد وغيرهم.
And there is no [hadd] for zina of one who is not legally responsible (non-mukallaf) with one who is legally responsible (mukallaf) at all. (And there is no [hadd] for zina of one who is not legally responsible with one who is legally responsible at all) meaning neither on this one nor on that one. And the hadith: 'Cursed is the one who approaches a woman in her anus' narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ahmad and others.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with a supporting hadith. The matn states that if a non-mukallaf (e.g., an insane person or a child who has not reached puberty) commits zina with a mukallaf (an adult sane person), then no hadd punishment falls on either of them. The commentary clarifies that neither party is liable for hadd. The hadith cited (li'an) is about anal intercourse and serves as a general deterrent but does not impose hadd for zina when one party lacks legal capacity. The ruling is unique to Hanafi fiqh, emphasizing that hadd requires both parties to be fully responsible.

Key Terms
غير مكلف (ghayr mukallaf): A person not legally responsible due to lack of sanity or puberty (e.g., child, insane).
مكلّفة (mukallafah): A legally responsible adult female (sane, post-puberty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Neither receives hadd.

Key Takeaway
No hadd is applied to either party in zina when one of them lacks legal capacity (ghayr mukallaf), because hadd requires mutual legal responsibility.

Hanafi Punishment for Sodomy: Ta'zir and Its Methods
Ruling on ta'zir for sodomy with specific punishment methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the punishment for sodomy and identify the specific ta'zir mechanisms described in the text, including their derivation from the story of Lut.

Core Idea
Sodomy is punished by ta'zir, not hadd, with methods inspired by the divine punishment of the people of Lut.

This lesson unpacks a brief but significant passage from the Hanafi tradition regarding the punishment for sodomy (liwatah). The text specifies a unique method of ta'zir—overturning from a height and stoning—and expands to include other discretionary punishments. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating how Hanafi jurists derived the punishment from the Quranic narrative and why they classified the offense as ta'zir rather than hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is liwatah (sodomy). According to Abu Hanifa, it is not subject to the fixed punishment (hadd) of zina. Instead, it falls under ta'zir—discretionary punishment determined by the judge.
This is the foundational distinction: ta'zir vs. hadd.
2
Examine the specific punishment mentioned
The passage states: 'overturning from a high place with following of stones.' This method is directly inspired by the Quranic account of how the people of Lut were destroyed—their towns lifted and overturned, and stones rained upon them.
The punishment is not arbitrary; it mirrors the divine punishment for the same sin.
3
Expand the scope of ta'zir methods
The commentary clarifies that ta'zir may include various forms: demolishing a wall on the offender, burning, imprisonment until repentance, and for habitual offenders, execution as a matter of policy (siyasah).
Ta'zir is flexible; the specific method is at the judge's discretion.
4
Understand the derivation (istinbat)
The proof is not a hadith or qiyas on zina, but the Quranic story itself. The jurists extracted a principle: since the people of Lut were punished by overturning and stones, a similar punishment can be used as ta'zir for the same act.
This is an example of using historical divine punishment as a guide for discretionary punishment.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Hanbali) may consider sodomy as equivalent to zina and apply the hadd of 100 lashes or stoning. The Hanafi school maintains ta'zir, which allows a broader range of punishments but does not require the strict evidentiary standards of hadd.
This difference has practical implications for conviction and sentencing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتنكيس من مكان مرتفع باتباع الأحجار، فعند أبي حنيفة له يعزر بأمثال هذه الأمور. [1] قوله : باتباع الأحجار ; مأخذه أن قوم لوط أهلكوا بذلك ، حيث حملت قراهم ونكست بهم، وأمطرت عليهم حجارة. [2] قوله : بأمثال هذه الأمور ; من هدم الجدار والتنكيس والإحراق والحبس إلى أن يتوب، بل لو اعتاد اللواطة قتل سياسة. كذا في «البحر».
And the overturning from a high place with following of stones. According to Abu Hanifa, he is ta'zir-ed with such matters. [1] His statement: 'with following of stones' — its source is that the people of Lut were destroyed by that, when their towns were lifted and overturned upon them, and stones rained upon them. [2] His statement: 'with such matters' — including demolition of a wall, overturning, burning, and imprisonment until he repents; but if he persists in sodomy, he is killed as a policy (siasah). As in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is a ruling on the punishment for sodomy (liwat). The matn says that the offender is turned upside down from a high place and then stones are thrown upon him. This method is derived from the punishment of the people of Lut. Abu Hanifa prescribes ta'zir (discretionary punishment) using similar means. The commentary elaborates that ta'zir can include demolishing a wall on him, burning, or imprisoning until repentance. If he habituales sodomy, he may be killed as a matter of siyasah (public policy). This is not hadd but ta'zir, and the specific methods are based on the story of Lut (alayhis salam).

Key Terms
التنكيس (al-tankis): Turning upside down from a height, a form of punishment derived from the destruction of the people of Lut.
اللواطة (al-liwatah): Sodomy, the act of the people of Lut.
قتل سياسة (qatl siyasah): Execution as a matter of policy for public interest, not a fixed punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) A hadith from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Sodomy in the Hanafi school is punished by ta'zir, not hadd, with methods inspired by the punishment of the people of Lut.

Hadd Dropped Due to Shubha When Marriage Is Claimed
Ruling: hadd dropped for both when one confesses zina and other claims marriage; mahr wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one party confesses to zina and the other claims marriage, and explain why hadd is dropped.

Core Idea
A marriage claim creates doubt (shubha) that drops hadd for both parties.

In hudud cases, confession is a strong proof. But what happens when one party confesses to zina while the other insists the intercourse was within a valid marriage? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses this conflict, showing how the Hanafi school prioritizes doubt (shubha) to avoid punishing what could be lawful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting statements
One party confesses to zina; the other claims marriage. Recognize that these are contradictory claims about the same act.
The confession is clear, but the claim of marriage offers an alternative legal characterization.
2
Apply the shubha principle
The claim of marriage, even if unproven, introduces doubt. In Hanafi law, any doubt (shubha) in the basis of the hadd results in its dropping (sqt al-hadd).
Shubha can arise from a factual claim or a legal ambiguity.
3
Determine the effect on both parties
Because shubha protects both parties, the hadd is dropped for both the confessor and the one claiming marriage.
The confession alone would normally establish hadd, but the shubha overrides it.
4
Identify the obligation of mahr
Despite the drop of hadd, the woman is entitled to mahr because the claim of marriage, even if doubtful, gives some right to her private part.
Mahr is wajib here as an honor (ta'zeeman) for the right of the vulva.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا إن أقر واحد به، والآخر بنكاح. قوله : ولا إن أقرّ ; يعني لو أقرّ الزاني أو الزانية بالزني وقال الآخر : كان الوطء بالتزوج سقط الحدّ عنهما ; لأنّ خبر النكاح يحتمل الصدق، فأورث ذلك شبهة، ويجب المهر تعظيماً له لحق البضع. كذا في «الهداية».
And not if one admits to it (zina) and the other (claims) marriage. His statement: 'And not if one admits' means if the male or female zani admits to zina and the other says: 'The intercourse was through marriage,' the hadd is dropped from both; because the news of marriage may be true, thus it creates a doubt (shubha), and the dower is obligatory to honor the right of the vulva. As in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This is a ruling on a procedural scenario in zina cases. If one party confesses to zina but the other claims that the intercourse was through a valid marriage, the hadd is dropped from both. The reason is that the claim of marriage could be true, which creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents the application of hadd. However, the dower (mahr) is still obligatory because the marriage claim, even if doubtful, gives some right to the woman regarding her private part. This ruling is from al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
أقر (aqarra): To confess (to zina).
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt or uncertainty that prevents the application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if one person confesses to zina and the other claims marriage, what happens to the hadd and mahr?
A) Hadd is applied to the confessor; mahr is not due.
B) Hadd is dropped for both; mahr becomes obligatory.
C) Hadd is dropped only if the confessor withdraws.
D) Both hadd and mahr are dropped.

Key Takeaway
Hadd is dropped when a claim of marriage creates doubt (shubha), but mahr is still due.

Killing an Amah During Zina: Cumulative Penalties
Ruling that killing an amah during zina incurs both hadd and monetary compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing an amah during zina and explain why both hadd and compensation are required.

Core Idea
Killing a slave woman during zina incurs both hadd and monetary compensation because each is a separate crime.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hudud chapter: if a person commits zina with a slave woman (amah) and then kills her, he is liable for both the hadd punishment for zina and the payment of her value (qimah) to her owner. The rationale is that he committed two distinct violations: one against the Sharīʿah (zina) and one against property (killing a slave). Understanding this application of cumulative penalties reinforces the principle that crimes are not merged when they arise from separate wrongful acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two offenses
The person committed zina (a hadd offense) and murder of a slave (a property crime). Note that the victim is an amah (female slave), not a free person.
If the victim were free, the penalty for killing would be diyah or qisas, not value.
2
Apply the rule of cumulative penalties
Hanafi fiqh treats these as independent crimes. The killer is not excused from hadd because he also killed, nor is he exempt from compensating the owner because he already faces hadd.
3
Compare with killing a free person during zina
If a free woman were killed during zina, the killer would face diyah or qisas, not value, because free persons are not property. Also, hadd for zina still applies if conditions are met.
The value (qimah) is specific to slaves.

Commentary
This is a ruling stating that if a person commits zina with a slave woman (amah) and then kills her, he incurs both the hadd punishment for zina and must pay her monetary value (ghirah) to her owner. The reason is that he committed two separate crimes: one against the Shari'ah (zina) and one against property (killing a slave). He is thus taken to account for each offense. This is a straightforward application of cumulative penalties.

Key Terms

القيمة (al-qimah): The monetary value of the slave woman, paid to her owner.

Ruling on the Khalfah: Exemption from Hadd but Liability for Qisas and Financial Penalty
Ruling on khalfah: no hadd, but qisas and financial penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a khalfah regarding hadd and qisas, and identify the underlying Hanafi principle of distinguishing between criminal liability categories.

Core Idea
The khalfah avoids hadd but owes qisas and money – showing that hadd is not the only punishment.

This brief passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents a ruling about a specific type of offender called 'khalfah'. Although the exact meaning of the term is ambiguous due to possible OCR corruption, the legal rule is clear: this person is not subject to hadd punishment, but is liable for qisas (retaliation) and must pay financial compensation. In Hanafi fiqh, this illustrates that not all offenses warrant the fixed corporal punishments; some cases fall under remedial or compensatory justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Determine who the khalfah is. Possibly a minor, an insane person, or a slave child. The term needs verification, but the ruling applies to a category of offender.
Due to OCR uncertainty, treat this as a placeholder for non-mukallaf offenders.
2
Determine the exempted punishment
The text states 'la yuhadd' – no hadd. Hadd are fixed punishments for specific crimes requiring full legal capacity.
Hadd includes penalties like amputation for theft or execution for murder.
3
Identify the applied punishments
The text says 'yuqtass wa yu'khadh bil-mal' – qisas and financial taking. Qisas is retributive justice (e.g., life for life), and financial penalty is compensatory.
Qisas requires intentional harm; financial penalty may apply when qisas is not possible.
4
Consider the legal reasoning
Why exempt from hadd but not from qisas/mal? Hadd requires legal capacity (mukallaf); qisas and mal are based on harm caused and can apply to non-mukallaf.
Financial liability does not require intention, only causation.
5
Apply the ruling
For a khalfah who commits a hadd crime, the judge imposes qisas and/or financial penalty instead of hadd.
This ruling is consistent with Hanafi principles on capacity.

The Caliph's Exemption from Hadd but Liability for Qisas and Financial Rights
Ruling with proof (talil) on caliph's criminal liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the caliph's liability for hadd versus qisas/financial claims and explain the legal rationale (talil) based on the distinction between divine and private rights.

Core Idea
The caliph is exempt from hadd but liable for qisas and debts because hudud are Allah's rights, private rights belong to individuals.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi rule regarding the head of state: the caliph is not subject to hadd punishment but is fully liable for qisas (retaliation) and financial obligations. The distinction hinges on the nature of the right: hudud are considered pure divine rights, while qisas and financial claims are private rights of individuals. Understanding this ruling provides insight into how Hanafi jurisprudence balances the ruler's role as executor of divine law with the inviolability of individual rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its two components
The passage states two rules: (1) the caliph is not given hadd punishment, and (2) he is subject to qisas and taken for financial liability. Identify each and note the contrasting treatment.
The ruling appears at the beginning: 'والخليفة لا يحد، ويُقْتَصُّ ويؤخذ بالمال'.
2
Locate the rationale for the hadd exemption
The text explains that the caliph is the possessor of the right of hadd on behalf of Allah, and he cannot enforce it on himself because it would be futile. Find and paraphrase this argument.
Key phrase: 'لأنه صاحب الحق نيابةً عن الله تعالى' and 'لا يمكنه أن يقيمه على نفسه؛ لأنه لا يفيد'.
3
Locate the rationale for qisas and financial liability
The text states that qisas and financial claims are private rights (حقوق العباد). The legitimate holder of the right (the heir or owner) can take it, either by empowering the caliph or by seeking help from the Muslim community. Identify this reasoning.
Key phrase: 'لأنَّ مَن له الحقُّ هو الوارث والمالك' and 'بخلاف حقوق العباد'.
4
Trace the talil from al-Hidayah
The commentary quotes al-Hidayah, which provides the core legal cause (illah): hudud are rights of Allah, and their enforcement is entrusted to the caliph alone; he cannot enforce it on himself. Private rights are different because the right-holder can claim them. Identify the distinction.
The dalil_block in the lesson summarizes this talil based on istihsan.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Understand that the rule applies only to the supreme Imam (caliph or equivalent). If the caliph commits a hadd crime, he is not punished by hadd; but if he kills someone or owes money, he must face qisas or pay. Recognize the practical difference.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and differs from other schools that may hold the ruler equally liable for all punishments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود الوطء الذي يوجب الحد
والخليفة لا يحد، ويُقْتَصُّ ويؤخذ بالمال

والخليفة لا يحد) ؛ لأنه صاحب الحق نيابةً عن الله تعالى، ويُقْتَصُّ ويؤخذ
بالمال) ؛ لأنَّ مَن له الحقُّ هو الوارث والمالك. والله أعلم.
قوله : والخليفة ؛ هو الإمام الذي ليس فوقه إمام، قال في «الهداية»: «لأنّ الحدود حق الله وإقامتها إليه لا إلى غيره ولا يمكنه أن يقيمه على نفسه ؛ لأنه لا يفيد، بخلاف حقوق العباد ؛ لأنه يستوفيه ولي الحق إما بتمكينه إياه، أو بالاستعانة بمنعة المسلمين، والقصاص والأموال منها.
The Book of Hadd Punishments: The sexual intercourse that necessitates the hadd. And the caliph is not given the hadd, and he is subject to qisas and taken for financial liability. (The caliph is not given the hadd) because he is the possessor of the right on behalf of Allah the Exalted, and he is subject to qisas and taken for financial liability because the one who has the right is the heir and the owner. And Allah knows best. His statement: 'al-Khalifa' is the imam who has no imam above him. He said in al-Hidayah: 'Because the hudud are the right of Allah, and their enforcement is entrusted to him, not to others, and he cannot enforce them upon himself because it is of no benefit, contrary to the rights of the subjects (human rights), because the guardian of the right takes it either by empowering him (the caliph) to do so, or by seeking assistance from the Muslim community. And qisas and financial rights are from among them (human rights).'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah discusses the exceptional status of the caliph regarding criminal punishments. It states that the caliph is not subject to hadd punishments because he acts as the representative of God for their enforcement, and it would be futile to punish himself. However, for claims involving private rights, such as qisas (retaliation for homicide or injury) and financial obligations, the caliph is fully liable because these rights belong to individuals (the heirs or the injured party). The proof cited from al-Hidayah clarifies that hudud are purely divine rights, while qisas and financial claims are personal rights of the people, which the caliph cannot claim exemption from. This reflects the Hanafi legal principle that the ruler is not above the law regarding private rights but has immunity regarding purely divine prescribed punishments due to his role as executor of God's law.

Key Terms
الخليفة (al-khalifah): The caliph; the supreme Imam with no Imam above him as the executor of hudud.
الحد (al-hadd): Prescribed punishment for certain crimes (e.g., zina, theft) that are rights of God.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation for homicide or injury; a private right of the victim or heirs.
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right of God; a legal claim that is not subject to waiver or compromise by individuals, typically referring to hudud.
حق العبد (haqq al-abd): A right of an individual; a personal legal claim that the holder may assert, waive, or compromise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because he can pay a fine instead.
D) Because hadd is only for common people.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the caliph is exempt from hadd because it is a divine right he enforces, but he is fully liable for private rights like qisas and financial claims.

Stale Testimony and Confession in Hudud: Rights of Allah vs Rights of Servants
Explains rulings on stale testimony for theft, drinking, and other hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stale testimony for hudud crimes, distinguish between testimony and confession, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the time period of taqadum.

Core Idea
Stale testimony for hudud still establishes financial rights but not hadd; confession is accepted.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position on taqadum (staleness) in hudud cases. It distinguishes between testimony and confession, and also addresses the time period that renders testimony stale. An intra-Hanafi dispute exists regarding the exact definition of taqadum for drinking and other crimes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substantive ruling for theft
The matn states that if witnesses testify to a stale theft, guarantee is established but not hadd. Why? Because it is a right of the servant, which does not lapse by staleness.
2
Contrast with confession
If a person confesses to a stale hadd crime, the hadd is applied (except drinking) because the preventer of testimony (possible enmity) does not apply to confession.
3
Define taqadum for drinking and other crimes
The matn states: for drinking, staleness is determined by the disappearance of the smell; for other crimes, by the passage of one month.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa left it to the judge's discretion. The most sound view (asahh) from Imam Muhammad fixes it at one month for all crimes. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) distinguished between drinking (smell) and others (month).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the smell disappears before a month, according to the two the testimony becomes stale immediately; according to Muhammad it remains valid until a month passes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضمن السرقة ) : أي إن شهدوا بالسرقة المتقادمة يثبت الضمان ; لأنَّهُ [۲] حق العبد ، وهو لا يسقط بالتقادم ، وعند الشَّافِعِي (۱) تقبل. ه
( وإن أقر به حدّ ) : أي إن أقرَّ بالحد المتقادم حدّ إلا في الشرب على ما يأتي ; لأنَّ المانع من قبولِ الشَّهادة أنه قد هيّجتُهُ على الشهادة عداوة حادثة، وهذا المعنى لا يوجد في الإقرار .

(وتقادم الشرب بزوال الرّيح ، ولغيره بمضي شهر)
[٤] قوله : وتقادم الشرب ; يعني في شرب المسكرِ إذا شهدوا بعد زوال الرائحة من فم الشارب لم تقبل.
[0] قوله : ولغيره ; أي غير الشرب من الزنا والسرقة وغيرهما، يكون بمضي الشهر متقادماً ، قال في «البحر » ) : اعلم أن التقادم عند الإمام الله مفوض إلى رأي القاضي في كل عصر ، لكنَّ الأصح ما عن محمد الله أنه مقدر بشهر، وهو مروي عنهما أيضاً، وقد اعتبره محمد الله في شرب الخمر أيضاً، وعندهما: وهو مقدر بزوال الرائحة.
And he guarantees the theft: meaning if they testify to the stale theft, the guarantee is established because it is a right of the servant and it is not voided by staleness. According to al-Shafi'i, it is accepted. And if he confesses to it, it is a hadd: meaning if he confesses to the stale hadd, it is applied except for drinking as will come, because the preventer of accepting testimony is that he may have been prompted by recent enmity, and this meaning is absent in confession. And staleness of drinking by the disappearance of the smell, and for other crimes by the passage of a month. [Commentary]: For drinking, if they testify after the smell has left the drinker's mouth, it is not accepted. For other crimes like zina and theft, etc., it becomes stale by the passage of a month. He said in al-Bahr: Know that staleness according to Imam Abu Hanifa is referred to the judge's opinion in every age, but the most sound is what is from Muhammad that it is estimated by a month, and it is narrated from the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well, and Muhammad considered it for drinking also, while according to the two it is estimated by the disappearance of the smell.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi rulings on stale testimony (taqadum) for hudud crimes. The first ruling: if witnesses testify to a theft that occurred long ago (stale), the thief is not subjected to hadd (amputation) but must pay financial compensation because the right of the owner (servant's right) does not become void by staleness. The commentary notes that according to al-Shafi'i, such testimony is accepted even for hadd, indicating an inter-madhhab difference. The second ruling: if a person confesses to a stale hadd crime, the hadd is applied (except for drinking) because the possible enmity that prevents accepting testimony does not apply to confession—a person does not bear enmity against himself. The third ruling concerns the definition of staleness: for drinking, the testimony is not accepted once the smell of alcohol from the mouth has disappeared; for other crimes (zina, theft, etc.), the testimony is considered stale after one month. The commentary includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa left the determination to the judge's discretion, but the most sound position (asahh) attributed to Imam Muhammad is that it is fixed at one month for all crimes, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two) hold that for drinking it is by the smell's disappearance and for other crimes by a month. The relied-upon position seems to be one month for all, though both views are narrated.

Key Terms
تقادم (taqadum): Staleness of a crime due to passage of time, making testimony for hadd unacceptable.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that can prevent the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Stale testimony for hudud crimes in the Hanafi school establishes only rights of servants, not hadd; the taqadum period is one month for all crimes per the most sound view.

Testimony for Hudud: Absence of the Accused in Zina vs Theft
Explains rulings on testimony for hudud when accused is absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony for zina and theft when the accused is absent, and explain the role of the claim (da'wa) as a condition in theft but not in zina.

Core Idea
In zina, hadd applies despite the woman's absence; in theft, the owner's claim is required.

This lesson examines two related rulings from the Book of Hudud: testimony for zina with an absent woman and testimony for theft from an absent owner. The Hanafi school draws a clear distinction based on whether a legal claim (da'wa) is required. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying hudud correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for zina with absent woman
The text states: 'If they testify for zina and she is absent, hadd (is applied).' Note that no claim from the woman is needed.
2
Identify the ruling for theft from absent person
The text states: 'and for theft from an absent person, no (hadd).' The testimony is not accepted because the owner is absent to make a claim.
3
Understand the reasoning for the distinction
The commentary explains: absence removes the claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. Zina is a pure right of God, while theft involves the right of the servant (property).
Theft mixes right of God and right of servant; the servant's claim initiates the hadd.
4
Address the objection about shubha
One might argue that the woman's absence creates a possibility of shubha (doubt) that should prevent hadd. The text answers: this is only a presumed shubha, not an actual one. Only actual shubha averts hadd.
The response uses the concept of 'shubha of shubha' (imaginary doubt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها
فإن شهدوا بزنا وهي غائبة حد، وبسرقة من غائب لا، ولو اختلف أربعة في زاويتي بيت
[١]قوله : حد...الخ; وجه الفرق : أنّ بالغيبة ينعدم الدعوى، وهي شرط في السرقة دون الزنا.
فإن قلت : عند غيبوبة المزنية احتمال دعواها الشبهة قائم فيجب أن لا يحد. قلت : هذا ليس وجوداً للشبهة ليسقط بها الحدّ، بل وجودها موهوم، فتكون شبهة الشبهة، والمعتبر في باب سقوط الحدود» هو الشبهة لا ما هو النازل عنها.
[٢] قوله : وبسرقة من غائب; أي شهدوا بأنه سرق مال فلان وهو غائب عن ذلك المقام.
[٣] قوله : الشرطية الدعوى في السرقة; يَرِدُ عليه أنه لو كانت الدعوى شرطاً في السرقة لَزِمَ أن يُحد في شهادة السرقة المتقادمة. وجوابه على ما يفهم من «الهداية» وحواشيها : إنَّ اشتراط الدعوى في السرقة إنما هي لثبوتِ المال لا لإقامة الحدّ، لأنه خالص حق الله، فيسقط الحد بالشهادة بالسرقة المتقادمة، ويجب المال.
[٤] قوله : ولو اختلف... الخ; يعني لو شهدت أربعة شهود بزناه، واختلفوا في زاويتي بيت واحد، فقال اثنان زنى بها في تلك الزاوية، وقال آخران : في زاوية أخرى، قبلت شهادتهم وأقيم الحد على الزاني، وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يُحَدَّ لاختلاف المكان حقيقة، وباختلافِ المكان يختلفُ الفعل، فلم يتم نصاب الشهادة على فعل واحد.
ووجه الاستحسان على ما في «الهداية» (۱) وغيرها : إن التوفيق ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء فعل الزنى في زاوية وانتهاؤه في زاوية أخرى بالحركة والاضطراب، وبأن يكون الزنى واقعا في وسط البيت، فيحسبه مَن في المقدَّم في المقدَّم، ومن في الآخر في الآخر.
Book of Hudud: Chapter on Testimony for Zina and Retraction Thereof. If they testify for zina and she is absent, hadd (is applied); and for theft from an absent person, no; and if four (witnesses) differ on two corners of a house. [Commentary]: The difference: because absence removes the claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. If it is said: When the woman is absent, the possibility of her claim of shubha exists, so he should not be punished. The answer: This is not an actual shubha that would avert the hadd; its existence is only imagined, so it is a shubha of shubha, and what is considered in averting hudud is actual shubha, not something lower. For theft from an absent person: they testify that he stole the property of so-and-so while he was absent from that place. The conditionality of claim in theft: An objection arises: if claim were a condition in theft, then it would necessitate that he be punished in the testimony for stale theft. The answer as understood from al-Hidayah and its commentaries: The stipulation of claim in theft is for establishing property, not for establishing hadd, because hadd is a pure right of God, so the hadd is dropped by testimony for stale theft, and the property is obligated. For the difference: meaning if four witnesses testify to his zina and they differ on two corners of a single house: two say he committed zina in that corner, and the other two say in another corner, their testimony is accepted and the hadd is applied to the fornicator. This is istihsan, while by qiyas he should not be punished because of the actual difference in place, and with difference of place the action differs, so the required number of witnesses for a single act is not completed. The basis of istihsan as in al-Hidayah and others: Reconciliation is possible because the beginning of the act of zina could be in one corner and its end in another due to movement and agitation, or because the zina occurred in the middle of the house, so those in the front consider it in the front and those in the back consider it in the back.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings concerning testimony for hudud with special circumstances. First ruling: if four witnesses testify to zina while the woman is absent (i.e., she is not present at the trial), the hadd punishment is still applied. The commentary explains the difference between zina and theft: absence eliminates the possibility of a claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. In theft, the owner must claim the property; if absent, no claim, so testimony is not accepted. But in zina, no claim from the woman is needed; the hadd is a right of God. The commentary also addresses an objection: one might argue that the woman's absence creates a shubha (doubt) that should prevent the hadd. The answer is that this is only a presumed shubha, not an actual one, and only actual shubha averts hadd. Second ruling: testimony for theft from an absent person is not accepted because the owner is not present to make a claim. Third ruling: if four witnesses see zina but disagree on the exact corner of the house where it occurred, their testimony is accepted and the hadd is applied by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would reject the testimony because the difference implies they saw different acts, so the required number of witnesses for one act is not met. But istihsan allows reconciliation by considering that the act may have spanned both corners due to movement, or that the witnesses observed from different angles and thus perceived different corners. This shows the Hanafi reliance on istihsan to achieve justice and avoid strict formalism.

Key Terms
دعوى (da'wa): Legal claim made by the plaintiff; in theft, it is a condition for accepting testimony, but not in zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if four witnesses testify to zina while the woman is absent, what is the ruling?
A) Hadd is applied
B) Hadd is not applied until she is present
C) The testimony is rejected
D) Only half the hadd is applied

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the presence of a claim (da'wa) is required for theft but not for zina due to the nature of the crime as a pure right of God.

Testimony for Zina when Witnesses Disagree on Location: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Explains istihsan ruling for witness disagreement on zina location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi application of istihsan to accept testimony for zina when witnesses differ on the exact location, and contrast it with the qiyas ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas to impose hadd when witnesses differ on location, reconciling their accounts.

This lesson focuses on a specific scenario: four witnesses testify to zina but disagree on the exact corner of the house where it occurred. The Hanafi school applies istihsan to accept the testimony and impose the hadd, overruling the strict qiyas that would reject it. Understanding this demonstrates the flexibility of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the qiyas ruling
Four witnesses see zina but differ on the corner. By strict qiyas, the testimony is rejected because difference in place implies difference in act, so the required number of witnesses for one act is not met.
2
Identify the effective cause (illa) in qiyas
The illa is that the place of the act is considered part of the act's identity. If place differs, the act differs.
This is a strict analogy.
3
Explain the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan allows reconciliation: the act may have spanned both corners due to movement, or witnesses may have viewed from different angles. Therefore, the testimony is accepted.
Istihsan prioritizes justice and practical reality over strict formal logic.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Schools that reject istihsan (e.g., Shafi'i) would apply qiyas and not impose hadd in such a scenario.
This is a legitimate area of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها
فإن شهدوا بزنا وهي غائبة حد، وبسرقة من غائب لا، ولو اختلف أربعة في زاويتي بيت
[١]قوله : حد...الخ; وجه الفرق : أنّ بالغيبة ينعدم الدعوى، وهي شرط في السرقة دون الزنا.
فإن قلت : عند غيبوبة المزنية احتمال دعواها الشبهة قائم فيجب أن لا يحد. قلت : هذا ليس وجوداً للشبهة ليسقط بها الحدّ، بل وجودها موهوم، فتكون شبهة الشبهة، والمعتبر في باب سقوط الحدود» هو الشبهة لا ما هو النازل عنها.
[٢] قوله : وبسرقة من غائب; أي شهدوا بأنه سرق مال فلان وهو غائب عن ذلك المقام.
[٣] قوله : الشرطية الدعوى في السرقة; يَرِدُ عليه أنه لو كانت الدعوى شرطاً في السرقة لَزِمَ أن يُحد في شهادة السرقة المتقادمة. وجوابه على ما يفهم من «الهداية» وحواشيها : إنَّ اشتراط الدعوى في السرقة إنما هي لثبوتِ المال لا لإقامة الحدّ، لأنه خالص حق الله، فيسقط الحد بالشهادة بالسرقة المتقادمة، ويجب المال.
[٤] قوله : ولو اختلف... الخ; يعني لو شهدت أربعة شهود بزناه، واختلفوا في زاويتي بيت واحد، فقال اثنان زنى بها في تلك الزاوية، وقال آخران : في زاوية أخرى، قبلت شهادتهم وأقيم الحد على الزاني، وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يُحَدَّ لاختلاف المكان حقيقة، وباختلافِ المكان يختلفُ الفعل، فلم يتم نصاب الشهادة على فعل واحد.
ووجه الاستحسان على ما في «الهداية» (۱) وغيرها : إن التوفيق ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء فعل الزنى في زاوية وانتهاؤه في زاوية أخرى بالحركة والاضطراب، وبأن يكون الزنى واقعا في وسط البيت، فيحسبه مَن في المقدَّم في المقدَّم، ومن في الآخر في الآخر.
Book of Hudud: Chapter on Testimony for Zina and Retraction Thereof. If they testify for zina and she is absent, hadd (is applied); and for theft from an absent person, no; and if four (witnesses) differ on two corners of a house. [Commentary]: The difference: because absence removes the claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. If it is said: When the woman is absent, the possibility of her claim of shubha exists, so he should not be punished. The answer: This is not an actual shubha that would avert the hadd; its existence is only imagined, so it is a shubha of shubha, and what is considered in averting hudud is actual shubha, not something lower. For theft from an absent person: they testify that he stole the property of so-and-so while he was absent from that place. The conditionality of claim in theft: An objection arises: if claim were a condition in theft, then it would necessitate that he be punished in the testimony for stale theft. The answer as understood from al-Hidayah and its commentaries: The stipulation of claim in theft is for establishing property, not for establishing hadd, because hadd is a pure right of God, so the hadd is dropped by testimony for stale theft, and the property is obligated. For the difference: meaning if four witnesses testify to his zina and they differ on two corners of a single house: two say he committed zina in that corner, and the other two say in another corner, their testimony is accepted and the hadd is applied to the fornicator. This is istihsan, while by qiyas he should not be punished because of the actual difference in place, and with difference of place the action differs, so the required number of witnesses for a single act is not completed. The basis of istihsan as in al-Hidayah and others: Reconciliation is possible because the beginning of the act of zina could be in one corner and its end in another due to movement and agitation, or because the zina occurred in the middle of the house, so those in the front consider it in the front and those in the back consider it in the back.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings concerning testimony for hudud with special circumstances. First ruling: if four witnesses testify to zina while the woman is absent (i.e., she is not present at the trial), the hadd punishment is still applied. The commentary explains the difference between zina and theft: absence eliminates the possibility of a claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. In theft, the owner must claim the property; if absent, no claim, so testimony is not accepted. But in zina, no claim from the woman is needed; the hadd is a right of God. The commentary also addresses an objection: one might argue that the woman's absence creates a shubha (doubt) that should prevent the hadd. The answer is that this is only a presumed shubha, not an actual one, and only actual shubha averts hadd. Second ruling: testimony for theft from an absent person is not accepted because the owner is not present to make a claim. Third ruling: if four witnesses see zina but disagree on the exact corner of the house where it occurred, their testimony is accepted and the hadd is applied by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would reject the testimony because the difference implies they saw different acts, so the required number of witnesses for one act is not met. But istihsan allows reconciliation by considering that the act may have spanned both corners due to movement, or that the witnesses observed from different angles and thus perceived different corners. This shows the Hanafi reliance on istihsan to achieve justice and avoid strict formalism.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling; here used to accept testimony despite location discrepancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas
B) Istihsan
C) Ijma
D) Consideration of public interest

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, istihsan can be used to reconcile witness discrepancies and impose hudud when strict analogy would block punishment.

Absence in Hudud Testimony: Zina vs Theft
Distinguishing condition of absence in zina vs theft testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the absence of the woman in zina testimony versus the absence of the claimant in theft testimony, and explain the underlying principle of da'wa (claim).

Core Idea
In Hanafi hudud, absence negates the claim for theft but not for zina.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi hudud law: how the absence of the affected party affects the application of hadd punishment for zina and theft. The text from the commentary on al-Hidayah presents the ruling and then defends it against possible objections, revealing the logical underpinning that a claim (da'wa) is a condition for theft but not for zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) testimony of zina where the woman is absent, and (2) testimony of theft where the property owner is absent.
Both involve the absence of a key figure.
2
State the ruling for each
For zina, the hadd is applied ('had'). For theft, the hadd is not applied ('la').
3
Locate the legal distinction
The commentator explains that the difference lies in the necessity of a claim (da'wa). A claim is a condition for theft but not for zina.
Absence negates the claim, which is why theft's hadd drops.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objection is raised: in zina, the absent woman could potentially claim a doubt (shubha), so why is the hadd still applied? The response: only actual doubt matters, not hypothetical doubt ('doubt of a doubt').
This sharpens the rule: shubha must be real, not imagined.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The hadd for theft is not applied when the claimant is absent, but the property right can still be established if the claimant later appears.
The condition of the claim is for establishing the property, not the hadd itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها
وهي غائبة حد، وبسرقة من غائب (لا)؛ الشرطية الدعوى في السرقة دون الزنا على ما يأتي الفرقُ في كتاب السرقة) إن شاء الله تعالى.
[١]قوله : حد...الخ ؛ وجه الفرق : أنّ بالغيبة ينعدم الدعوى ، وهي شرط في السرقة دون الزنا. فإن قلت : عند غيبوبة المزنية احتمال دعواها الشبهة قائم فيجب أن لا يحد. قلت : هذا ليس وجوداً للشبهة ليسقط بها الحدّ، بل وجودها موهوم، فتكون شبهة الشبهة، والمعتبر في باب سقوط الحدود» هو الشبهة لا ما هو النازل عنها. [٢] قوله : وبسرقة من غائب ؛ أي شهدوا بأنه سرق مال فلان وهو غائب عن ذلك المقام.
(۳) قوله : الشرطية الدعوى في السرقة ؛ يَرِدُ عليه أنه لو كانت الدعوى شرطاً في السرقة لَزِمَ أن يُحد في شهادة السرقة المتقادمة. وجوابه عـلـى مـا يفهم من «الهداية» وحواشيها : إنَّ اشتراط الدعوى في السرقة إنما هي لثبوتِ المال لا لإقامة الحدّ ، لأنه خالص حق الله ، فيسقط الحد بالشهادة بالسرقة المتقادمة، ويجب المال.
Book of Hudud: Chapter on Testimony of Zina and Retraction. And if she is absent, hadd [is applied], and by theft from an absent person, no [hadd]; the condition of the claim is in theft without zina, as the difference will come in the Book of Theft, God willing. [1] He said: 'hadd...' etc.; the face of the difference: that by absence the claim is absent, and it is a condition in theft without zina. If you say: at the absence of the woman, the possibility of her claiming a doubt exists, so it should not be hadd. I say: this is not an existence of doubt to drop the hadd by it, rather its existence is imagined, so it is a doubt of a doubt, and what is considered in the chapter of dropping hudud is the doubt not what is below it. [2] He said: 'and by theft from an absent person'; i.e., they testified that he stole the property of so-and-so while he was absent from that place. (3) He said: 'the condition of the claim in theft'; it is objected that if the claim were a condition in theft, it would necessitate that hadd be applied in testimony of theft that is outdated. And its answer according to what is understood from al-Hidayah and its glosses: indeed the condition of the claim in theft is only for the establishment of the property, not for the establishment of the hadd, because it is purely the right of Allah, so the hadd is dropped by testimony of outdated theft, and the property is obligatory.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
The passage is a ruling with proof distinguishing the effect of the absence of the subject in zina versus theft for hudud testimony. The matn states: if the woman is absent (gha'ibah), the hadd penalty for zina is still applied; but if the thief is absent, the hadd for theft is not applied. The commentary explains the rationale: the absence negates the legal claim (da'wa), which is a condition for theft but not for zina. A possible objection is raised: at the woman's absence, there is a possibility that she might claim a doubt (shubha), which would drop the hadd. The response is that this possibility is only a hypothetical doubt (shubhat al-shubha), not an actual doubt, and only actual doubts are considered for dropping hudud. Another objection: if a claim were required for theft, then a testimony about an old theft would necessitate hadd, but the answer clarifies that the condition of a claim is for establishing the property right, not for the hadd itself, which is a pure right of Allah.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): The prescribed corporal punishment for certain crimes as a right of Allah.
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The legal claim or demand by the plaintiff that initiates the case.
الشبهة (al-shubha): A legal doubt that can drop the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage
