Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the absence of the woman in zina does not prevent the hadd, but the absence of the claimant in theft does prevent the hadd because a claim is a condition unique to theft.

Istihsan Overriding Qiyas in Witness Disagreement
Applying istihsan to accept testimony despite disagreement on corner of house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to cases where witness testimony appears contradictory due to location details.

Core Idea
Istihsan allows accepting testimony despite apparent contradiction if reconciliation (tawfiq) is plausible.

The Hanafi school uses istihsan to achieve justice in hudud cases. This lesson examines a ruling where four witnesses disagree on the exact corner of a house for zina, yet their testimony is accepted. By understanding the reasoning, you will see how Hanafi fiqh prioritizes practical reconciliation over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qiyas Objection
First, articulate the strict qiyas argument: since the witnesses differ on the location, the act may be different, so the required four witnesses for one act are not met. This would lead to no hadd.
This is the default ruling if only qiyas were applied.
2
Understand the Istihsan Argument
Learn the istihsan reasoning: reconciliation (tawfiq) is possible because the act may have spanned corners due to movement, or the witnesses may have perceived the same act from different angles. Thus, they are testifying to one act.
Istihsan is a departure from qiyas for a more suitable outcome.
3
Reconcile the Two Positions
The Hanafi school adopts istihsan: testimony is accepted, hadd is applied. This shows that when contradiction can be reasonably resolved, the law prefers to uphold the testimony to enforce the divine penalty.
The burden is on the judge to determine if reconciliation is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلف أربعة في زاويتي بيت
[٤] قوله : ولو اختلف... الخ ؛ يعني لو شهدت أربعة شهود بزناه، واختلفوا في زاويتي بيت واحد، فقال اثنان زنى بها في تلك الزاوية، وقال آخران : في زاوية أخرى، قبلت شهادتهم وأقيم الحد على الزاني، وهذا استحسان، والقياس أن لا يُحَدَّ لاختلاف المكان حقيقة، وباختلافِ المكان يختلفُ الفعل، فلم يتم نصاب الشهادة على فعل واحد.
ووجه الاستحسان على ما في «الهداية» (۱) وغيرها : إن التوفيق ممكن بأن يكون ابتداء فعل الزنى في زاوية وانتهاؤه في زاوية أخرى بالحركة والاضطراب، وبأن يكون الزنى واقعا في وسط البيت، فيحسبه مَن في المقدَّم في المقدَّم، ومن في المؤَخَّر فى المؤخّر، فيشهد كل حسبما ظنه.
And if four differ about two corners of a house... [4] He said: 'and if four differ...' etc.; meaning: if four witnesses testify to his zina, and they differ about two corners of one house, so two said he committed zina with her in that corner, and two others said in another corner, their testimony is accepted and the hadd is established on the fornicator, and this is istihsan, and by qiyas he should not be hadded because of the disagreement in place in reality, and with the difference of place the act differs, so the complete number of testimony on one act is not fulfilled. And the face of istihsan according to what is in al-Hidayah and others: indeed reconciliation is possible in that the beginning of the act of zina may be in a corner and its end in another corner due to movement and agitation, and in that the zina may occur in the middle of the house, so the one in the front counts it as in the front, and the one in the back in the back, so each testifies according to what he presumed.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof specifically an application of istihsan overriding qiyas. The matn states that if four witnesses testify to zina but disagree on which corner of the house it occurred, the testimony is accepted by istihsan. The commentator explains: by qiyas, the disagreement would invalidate the testimony because the act is one physical event; differing locations imply different acts. However, istihsan permits acceptance because reconciliation (tawfiq) is possible: the act could have started in one corner and ended in another due to motion, or the actual act could have been in the middle, with each witness perceiving it from their perspective. Thus, the witnesses are testifying to the same act, albeit from different vantage points. This is a clear example of the Hanafi use of istihsan to achieve a just and practical outcome.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that deviates from strict qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.
توفيق (tawfiq): Reconciliation or harmonization of seemingly contradictory evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Istihsan permits accepting witness testimony despite minor disagreement if the contradiction can be reasonably reconciled.

Confession to Zina and Ignorance of the Woman's Identity
Ruling on confessor who does not know the woman's identity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a confessor who is ignorant of the woman's identity and explain the underlying reasoning that confession itself negates shubha.

Core Idea
A confessor's ignorance of the woman's identity does not prevent hadd because the confession proves no lawful relationship existed.

This lesson examines a specific hudud scenario: a person confesses to zina but claims not to know the woman. According to the Hanafi school, the hadd is still applied. The reasoning relies on the principle that a person would not confess if there were a genuine doubt (shubha) about the woman's permissibility—such as her being his wife or slave-concubine. This principle distinguishes confession from testimony and underscores the strength of iqrar as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is confessing to zina while claiming ignorance of the woman. The ruling is that the hadd is applied.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the qa'idah (principle): a person does not confess falsely nor in a state of doubt. The text states: 'لأن الإنسان كما لا يُقرّ على نفسه كاذباً لا يُقِرُّ على نفسه حال الاشتباه أيضاً'.
This is a rational principle accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The confession itself indicates that the confessor knew the woman was a stranger (ajnabiyya). If there had been a shubha (e.g., she was his wife), he would not have confessed. Thus, his claim of ignorance refers only to name/lineage, not to legal status.
The text contrasts this with a witness, who may testify despite uncertainty.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The position is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may require the confessor to identify the woman for the confession to be valid. The Hanafi response is that the confession's strength precludes such a requirement.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is to apply the hadd. No compensation or alternative is needed.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أقر بزنا وجَهلَها حد
[1] قوله : أو أقرّ ; يعني أقرّ الزاني بالزنى وقال : لا أعلم أو لا أعرف المزنية فيحدّ في هذه الصورة، ولا يضرّ جهلُ المزنيّة ؛ لأنه لا يخفى عليه من له فيها شبهة، فلو كانت امرأته أو أم ولده أو كان الأمر مشتبهاً عليه، لم يقر بذلك ؛ لأن الإنسان كما لا يُقرّ على نفسه كاذباً لا يُقِرُّ على نفسه حال الاشتباه أيضاً.
فلما أقر بالزني كان فرع علمه أنّها لم تشتبه عليه، فيكون معنى قوله : لم أعرفها ؛ أي باسمها ونسبها ، ولكن علمت أنها أجنبية، وهذا بخلاف الشاهد، فإنّه يجوز أن يشهد على من تشتبه عليه، فلا يكون قول الشاهد : لا أعرفها موجباً للحد.
[2] قوله : إذ التوفيق ; هذا التوفيق ونحوه إنّما يتيسر في بيت صغير جداً كما أشرنا إليه، وكذا وضع الغزي في تنوير الأبصار»: المسألة فيه، فإنّه لو كان كبيراً لا يتيسر فيه هذا التوفيق لم تقبل الشهادة.
[٣]قوله : ممكن ; لا يقال : هذا توفيق لإقامة الحد والواجب درؤه لأنا نقول : مثلُ هذا التوفيق مشروع صيانة للقضاء عن التعطيل، كيف وفي شهادة أربعة جامعــة لشرائطها يحتمل أن يكون ما رآه واحدٌ في وقت وما رآه آخر في وقت آخر، لكنه يحمل على الاتحاد، وإن لم ينصوا عليه. كذا في «الفتح»(۲). [٤]قوله : وجهل المقر ; هذه إضافة إلى الفاعل ومفعوله : المزنية، وهذا متعلّق بالمسألة الثانية.
[0]قوله : لا يخفى عليه ; الصواب : لم تخف عليه ; لأنّ كلمة «لو» لانتفاء الجزاء انتفاء الشرط في الزمان الماضي، وأمثالُ هذه المساهلات اللفظية كثيرة في عباراتِ (۱) «فتح القدير»(٥ : ٢٨٤). (۲) «فتح القدير (٥ : ١٨٧).
Or if he confessed to zina and was ignorant of her, hadd [applied]. [1] He said: 'or if he confessed'; meaning the fornicator confessed to zina and said: I do not know or I do not recognize the woman, so he is hadded in this case, and his ignorance of the woman does not harm him; because it is not hidden from him who has a doubt regarding her, so if she were his wife or his umm walad or the matter were dubious to him, he would not confess to that; because just as a person does not confess falsely against himself, he also does not confess against himself in a state of doubt. So when he confessed to zina, it is a branch of his knowledge that she was not dubious to him, so the meaning of his saying 'I do not know her' is by name and lineage, but he knew she was a stranger, and this differs from the witness, for it is permissible for him to testify about someone who is dubious to him, so the witness's saying 'I do not know her' does not necessitate hadd. [2] He said: 'since reconciliation is possible'; this reconciliation and the like is only possible in a very small house as we pointed out, and likewise al-Ghazzi placed in Tanwir al-Absar: the issue is in it, for if it were large, this reconciliation would not be possible, and the testimony would not be accepted. [3] He said: 'possible'; it cannot be said: this is a reconciliation to establish the hadd while the duty is to ward it off, because we say: such reconciliation is legislated to preserve the judiciary from being disrupted. [4] He said: 'and the ignorance of the confessor'; this is an addition to the subject and object: the woman, and this relates to the second issue. [0] He said: 'it is not hidden from him'; the correct is 'it was not hidden from him'; because the word 'law' is for negation of the consequent by negation of the condition in past time, and such verbal laxities are many in the expressions...
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding a person who confesses to zina but claims ignorance of the woman's identity. The matn states that he is still subject to hadd. The commentary explains that his ignorance does not harm his confession because a person would not confess if there were any valid doubt (shubha) regarding the woman, such as if she were his wife or slave-concubine (umm walad). By confessing, he implicitly affirms that the woman was not one of those with whom he had a lawful relationship. Thus, his statement 'I do not know her' is interpreted to mean he does not know her name or lineage, but he knows she is a stranger (ajnabiyya). This differs from a witness, who may testify about someone even if he has a doubt, so a witness's ignorance does not lead to hadd. The commentary also includes a cross-reference to the previous lesson about reconciliation (tawfiq) in the case of differing witnesses, noting that such reconciliation is only possible in a very small house. The text also addresses a possible objection: that reconciliation should not be used to establish hadd because the principle is to ward off hudud. The response is that such reconciliation is legislated to prevent the court from being rendered ineffective.

Key Terms
المقر (al-muqirr): The person who confesses (to a crime).
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt that can affect the application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The hadd is applied only if the woman confirms.
D) The hadd is not applied unless there are four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A valid confession to zina is sufficient for hadd even if the confessor is ignorant of the woman's identity, because the confession itself removes any doubt of a lawful relationship.

The Confessor's Ignorance of the Woman: Hadd Still Applied
Explaining the ruling when a confessor claims ignorance of the woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a confessor's ignorance of the woman does not avert the hadd, and explain the reasoning using the principle that no one confesses falsely or in doubt.

Core Idea
Confession to zina implies no genuine doubt; ignorance of the woman's identity does not create a shubha.

When a person confesses to zina but claims not to know the woman, a question arises: does this ignorance create doubt (shubha) that averts the hadd punishment? The Hanafi school holds that the confession itself negates any genuine doubt, because a rational person would not confess if there were a real uncertainty about the woman being lawful. In this lesson, we examine the text of al-Hidayah's commentary and trace the legal reasoning that leads to this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: 'Or he confessed to zina and was ignorant of her, then he is punished.' The ruling is clear: the confessor is subject to hadd despite his claim of ignorance.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The commentator provides a rational proof: 'A person does not confess falsely against himself, nor does he confess in a state of doubt.' This is the core dalil for the ruling.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof), not a scriptural text.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The proof implies that if the confessor had any genuine shubha (e.g., she might be his wife), he would not confess. Therefore, his confession is evidence that he knew she was a stranger. His claim 'I do not know her' means only that he does not know her name, not that he is unsure of her illegality.
4
Contrast with a Witness
The commentator distinguishes between a confessor and a witness. A witness may testify even if he is uncertain about the woman's identity, because his testimony is based on what he saw, not on his own admission. Hence, a witness's claim of ignorance would negate the hadd. This contrast sharpens the confessor's unique position.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools might accept ignorance as a doubt that averts hadd. The Hanafi position rests on the principle that the confessor's admission is stronger than a witness's uncertainty.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn that if a person confesses to zina but claims ignorance of the woman, he is still subject to hadd (the prescribed punishment). The commentator explains that the confessor's ignorance does not prevent the hadd because his very confession implies that he knows she is not his wife or his concubine (umm walad) – otherwise he would not have confessed. The reasoning is that a person would not falsely admit to something, nor would he admit when there is a genuine doubt (shubha). Therefore, his claim of ignorance is understood as ignorance of her name and lineage, not of her being a lawful partner. This differs from a witness (shahid), who may testify even if he is uncertain about the woman's identity, so his claim of ignorance would negate the hadd. The text also discusses the possibility of reconciling testimonies that seem contradictory regarding the location of the act, especially in a very small room. Such reconciliation is permissible to avoid invalidating the hadd and to keep the judicial process functional. The commentator also corrects a grammatical error in the phrase 'la yakhfa 'alayhi' to 'lam takhfa 'alayhi' due to the use of 'law' for past contrary-to-fact conditions.

Key Terms
جهل المقر (jahl al-muqirr): The confessor's claim of ignorance regarding the woman he committed zina with.
المزنية (al-mazniyya): The woman with whom zina was committed; the object of the act.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that averts the hadd punishment, e.g., if the man believed she was his wife.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: a confessor's ignorance of the woman does not avert hadd because his confession itself eliminates the possibility of genuine doubt.

Scenarios That Avert Hadd Due to Witness Irregularities
Listing scenarios where witness contradictions negate hadd for zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six scenarios that prevent hadd for zina under Hanafi law and explain the legal basis for each.

Core Idea
Any doubt—whether in testimony or possibility of lawful intercourse—averts the hadd punishment.

The hadd punishment for zina is severe, and the Shari'ah requires absolute certainty before imposing it. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya lists six situations where the testimony of witnesses fails to meet the required standard, either because of contradictions, physical impossibility, or lack of credibility. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for applying the principle that hadd is averted by doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Recognize that each scenario creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents hadd, either because the act might not be zina or because the evidence is unreliable. The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Avert the hudud by doubts.'
2
Categorize the scenarios
Group the six scenarios into three types: (a) contradictions about the act itself (volition, location, time vs. place), (b) physical impossibility (virgin, ratqa, qarna), and (c) witness inadequacy (fasiq, indirect testimony).
3
Analyze the logical basis for each
For each scenario, explain why doubt arises. For example, disagreement on location suggests the witnesses did not observe the same event; a virgin's testimony contradicts physical reality; sinful witnesses lack the required 'adala.
4
Apply the ruling to new fact patterns
Given a hypothetical, determine which scenario (if any) applies and conclude whether hadd is imposed. Practice with variations such as partial agreements or different combinations of contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها
فإن شهدوا كذلك، أو اختلفوا في طوعِها، أو بلد زناه، أو اتفق حجتاه في وقته واختلفا في بلده أو شهدوا بزنا وهي بكر، أو هم فسقة، أو هم شهود على شهود لم يحدّ أحد، وإن شَهدَ الأصول أيضا بعدهم
واعلم أن في هذه الصور لا يحد أحدٌ لا المشهود عليهما بالزنا، ولا الشهود القذف. فقوله : : وإن شهدوا كذلك ؛ أي " شهدوا وجَهلُـوا الموطوءة لا حـد علـى المشهود عليه ؛ لاحتمال أن تكون المرأة زوجتَهُ أو أمته، ولا على الشهود ؛ لوجود أربعة شهداء. الشارح له في هذا الشرح، وفي «التوضيح» ومتنه «التنقيح»، ولكن لما كان المقصود واضحاً أعرضنا عن ذكرها في هذه الحاشية إلا نادراً. [١) قوله : في طَوْعها ؛ - بالفتح - مقابل الإكراه ؛ أي اختلف الشهود في رضى الموطوءة. [٢] قوله : أو اتفق ؛ يعني اتفقت الشهود الأربعة على وقتِ الزنى وغيره واختلفوا في بلده. [٦] قوله : بعدهم ؛ أي بعد شهادة الفروع : أي الشهود على الشهود. [۷] قوله : أي ؛ إشارة إلى أن قوله : «كذلك» إشارة إلى ما دل عليه قوله : وجهلها». [۸]قوله : لاحتمال.... الخ ; لو قال : لاحتمال أن يكون له فيها شبهة لكان أولى.
Chapter of Hudud, Section on Testimony for Zina and Retraction Therefrom
If they testified in that manner, or they differed about her volition, or about the city of her zina, or both agreed on its time and differed about its city, or they testified about zina while she was a virgin, or they were sinners, or they were witnesses upon witnesses – no one is punished, even if the original witnesses also testify after them.
Know that in these scenarios no one is punished: neither the two persons accused of zina, nor the witnesses for qadhf (false accusation). His statement: 'If they testified in that manner' means they testified while being ignorant of the woman; there is no hadd on the accused because of the possibility that the woman is his wife or his slave-woman, and no hadd on the witnesses because there are four witnesses. The commentator has dealt with this in this commentary and in al-Tawdih and its text al-Tanqih, but since the intent is clear, we have refrained from mentioning them in this marginalia except rarely. [1] His statement: 'in her volition' – with a fatha, opposite of coercion, meaning the witnesses differed about the woman's consent. [2] His statement: 'or both agreed' means the four witnesses agreed on the time of zina etc. and differed about its city. [3] His statement: 'a virgin' – likewise if he knows she is a ratqa' or qarna', with whom intercourse is impossible. [4] His statement: 'sinners' – with fatha, plural of fasiq, like talaba plural of talib, meaning the witnesses are sinful and not acceptable testimony. [0] His statement: 'or they are witnesses upon witnesses' – its form is that the witnesses of zina who saw the act with their own eyes do not attend the court due to an excuse, so others testify to their testimony, and then they testify before the judge concerning their testimony. [6] His statement: 'after them' means after the testimony of the branches (i.e., the witnesses upon witnesses). [7] His statement: 'that' – an indication that his statement 'thus' refers to what his statement 'and her ignorance' indicated. [8] His statement: 'because of the possibility... etc.' – if he had said 'because of the possibility that he has a doubt regarding her', it would have been better.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage lists several scenarios where the hadd punishment for zina is not imposed on either the accused or the witnesses. The matn states that if the witnesses testify while ignorant of the woman, or if they differ on whether she consented, or on the location of the act, or if they agree on the time but differ on the city, or if they testify that she was a virgin (making the act impossible), or if the witnesses themselves are sinful (fasiq) and thus unacceptable, or if the testimony is indirect (shuhud 'ala shuhud) – then no one is punished. The commentary explains each scenario: the reason for not punishing the accused is the possibility (ihtimal) that the woman was his wife or slave; the reason for not punishing the witnesses is that there are still four testimonies (even if contradictory). The commentator also notes that this section overlaps with al-Tawdih and al-Tanqih, but he omits repetition. Each scenario is clarified: difference on volition means some said she consented, others said she was coerced; difference on location means the witnesses could not agree on the city; if she is a virgin or has a physical impediment, intercourse is impossible, so the testimony is false; sinful witnesses are not credible; indirect testimony means that the original witnesses did not appear in court, so their testimony is transmitted by others – this is insufficient for hadd. The commentator also notes that the phrase 'thus' refers back to the earlier ruling about ignorance of the woman.

Key Terms
شهود على شهود (shuhud 'ala shuhud): Indirect witnesses who testify based on the testimony of the original eyewitnesses.
فسقة (fasaqa): Sinners; witnesses who are known for major sins and thus their testimony is rejected in hadd cases.
بكر (bikr): A virgin; testimony of zina against a virgin is rejected because intercourse is impossible without breaking the hymen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadd is imposed because they agree on the essential elements.
B) The hadd is not imposed because of the disagreement on location.
C) The witnesses are punished for false accusation.
D) The case is postponed until they agree.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for zina is averted whenever witness testimony contains contradictions, physical impossibility, or credibility issues that create legal doubt.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Consent Split in Zina Testimony
Rulings on witness discrepancies in zina testimony and intra-Hanafi dispute on consent split

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on witness disagreement regarding consent in zinā testimony and apply the rule to a scenario where witnesses split on consent.

Core Idea
Consent contradiction splits the act: Abu Hanifa drops hadd for both; Sahibayn punish the man only.

In this lesson, we examine a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning witness testimony for zinā when the witnesses disagree about the woman's consent. The rule of 'doubt drops the hadd' (al-ḥadd yudra'u bi al-shubuhāt) is central, but the Sahibayn interpret the disagreement differently. By understanding the reasoning of each imam, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school handles conflicting evidence in hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Four witnesses testify to an act of zinā. Two say the woman was willing (ṭā'i'a) and two say she was coerced (mukraha). Determine what each version implies for liability.
The passage also lists other scenarios where hadd is dropped (e.g., unknown woman, virgin, fāsiq witnesses), but the focus here is the consent split.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd is applied to either the man or the woman because the witnesses contradict each other on a fundamental attribute of the act.
His dalīl: the act is one, cannot be both voluntary and coerced, so the testimony is defective for both.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalīl
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the man is punished because all four agree he committed zinā; the woman is not punished because her consent is disputed.
They see the coercion claim as an additional allegation that does not negate the agreement on the act itself.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The text presents Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: the legal description of the act changes based on consent; since the witnesses assign contradictory attributes, the testimony fails entirely.
An objection is raised about the possibility of part volition/part coercion, but it is rebutted by considering the beginning of the act.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, both parties go free. Under the Sahibayn, the man receives the hadd (stoning/lashing) and the woman is acquitted.
The text does not explicitly choose a muftā bihī, but the detailed defense of Abu Hanifa's view indicates support for his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١] قوله في طوعها بالفتح مقابل الإكراه أي اختلف الشهود في رضى الموطوءة. [٢] قوله أو اتفق يعني اتفقت الشهود الأربعة على وقت الزنى وغيره واختلفوا في بلده. [٣] قوله بكر وكذا لو علم أنها رتقاء أو قرناء لا يمكن الجماع بها. [٤] قوله فسقة بفتحات جمع فاسق كطلبة جمع طالب يعني إن الشهود فاسقون غير مقبولي الشهادة. [٥] قوله أو هم شهود على شهود صورته أن لا يحضر شهود الزنا الذين شاهدوا الزنى بأعينهم مجلس الحاكم لعذر فيشهدوا على شهادتهم غيرهم فشهدوا عند الحاكم على شهادتهم. [٦] قوله بعدهم أي بعد شهادة الفروع أي الشهود على الشهود. [٧] قوله أي إشارة إلى أن قوله كذلك إشارة إلى ما دل عليه قوله وجهلها. [٨] قوله لاحتمال الخ لو قال لاحتمال أن يكون له فيها شبهة لكان أولى. وإن شهد أربعة وقال اثنان منها كانت طائعة واثنان منهما كانت مكرهة فلا حد عليهما عند أبي حنيفة. وعندهما يحد الرجل لاتفاق الأربعة على زناه لا المرأة للاختلاف في طوعها. وله إن الفعل المشهود به إن كان واحداً فبعضهم كاذب لأن الفعل الواحد لا يكون بطوعها وكرها. [١] قوله منها الأولى في الموضعين منهم ولعل التأنيث نظراً إلى أن الشهود جمع وهو في حكم التأنيث أو نظراً إلى لفظ أربعة والحاصل أنه شهد اثنان بأن المرأة كانت طائعة أي راضية بفعله وقال آخران لم تكن طائعة بل أكرهها الرجل. [٢] قوله يحد الرجل فإن الشهود شهدوا بزناء طائعاً بل زاد اثنان منهم جناية أخرى وهي الإكراه. [٣] قوله لا المرأة أي لا تحد المرأة لأن رضاها شرط تحقق الموجب في حقها ولم يثبت لاختلافهما. [٤] قوله وله الخ حاصله أنه لما اختلفت الشهود اختلف المشهود به لأن الزنا فعل واحد يقوم بالرجل والمرأة وكل فعل واحد يقوم بهما لا يتصف بوصفين متضادين وهؤلاء أثبتوا له وصفين متضادين فإن الطوع يوجب اشتراكهما في الزنا والكره يوجب انفراد الرجل به واجتماعهما متعذر فكان كل واحد منهما خلاف الآخر فاختلف المشهود به ولم يتم على كل منهما نصاب الشهادة كذا في العناية. [٥] قوله لا يكون بطوعها وكرهها يرد عليه أنه يجوز أن يكون بعضه بالطوع وبعضه بالكره فأمكن التوفيق ولم يلزم كذب بعضهم. ويجاب عنه بأن الاعتبار لأول الفعل في الطوع والكره فإذا انعقد موجباً للحد لا ينقلب غير موجب للحد وكذا بالعكس.
The Book of Hudud, Chapter on Testimony of Zina and Retraction Therefrom. If they testify thus, or differ regarding her consent, or the location of her zinā, or if two of them agree on its time and differ on its location, or they testify to zinā while she is a virgin, or they are immoral (fāsiq), or they are witnesses upon witnesses, no one is to be punished with hadd, even if the original witnesses (al-usūl) testify after them. Know that in these scenarios no one is punished—neither the ones accused of zinā, nor the witnesses for qadhf. His saying: 'If they testify thus' means they testify without knowing the woman; there is no hadd on the accused because it is possible the woman is his wife or slave-girl, and no hadd on the witnesses because there are four witnesses. He explained this in this commentary and in al-Tawḍīḥ and its matn al-Tanqīḥ, but since the meaning is clear we have refrained from mentioning it in this gloss except rarely. [1] His saying: 'regarding her consent'—with fatḥa—as opposed to coercion; meaning the witnesses differed on the woman's willingness. [2] His saying: 'or agree' means all four witnesses agreed on the time of zinā and other details but differed on its location. [3] His saying: 'virgin'—and likewise if they know she has a closed vagina (ratqā') or a fleshy obstruction (qarnā') preventing intercourse. [4] His saying: 'immoral'—with fatḥāt, plural of fāsiq, like ṭalaba plural of ṭālib—means the witnesses are immoral and unacceptable in testimony. [5] His saying: 'or they are witnesses upon witnesses'—its form is that the zinā witnesses who saw the act with their own eyes do not attend the judge's session due to an excuse, so others testify to their testimony, and they testify before the judge to their testimony. [6] His saying: 'after them' means after the testimony of the branch witnesses (al-furū'), i.e., the witnesses upon witnesses. [7] His saying: 'which is' indicates that his saying 'thus' refers to what is indicated by his saying 'and not knowing her'. [8] His saying: 'because of the possibility... etc.'—would be better if he said: 'because of the possibility that he has a legal right (shubha) over her.' And if four witness, and two of them say: she was willing (ṭā'i'a), and two of them say: she was coerced (mukraha), then there is no hadd on either of them according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the man is to be punished because of the agreement of the four on his zinā, but not the woman because of the disagreement on her consent. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof: If the act witnessed is one and the same, then some of them are lying, because a single act cannot be both voluntary and coerced. [1] His saying: 'from them'—the better phrasing in both places is 'from them' (minhum), and perhaps the feminine is because the witnesses are a group, which is treated as feminine, or it refers to the word 'four'. The summary: two witnesses stated that the woman was willing (i.e., consenting to his act), and the other two said she was not willing but rather the man coerced her. [2] His saying: 'the man is punished'—because the witnesses testified to zinā while willing, and two added another crime (al-ikrāh). [3] His saying: 'not the woman' means the woman is not punished because her consent is a condition for the occurrence of the legal cause (mūjib) in her right, and it is not established due to their disagreement. [4] His saying: 'and his proof... etc.'—its summary: when the witnesses disagreed, the subject of testimony differed; because zinā is a single act involving both man and woman, and every single act involving both cannot be described with two contradictory attributes. These witnesses attributed to it two contradictory attributes: willingness requires their partnership in zinā, while coercion requires the man alone to be guilty, and their combination is impossible. Thus, each group contradicted the other, so the subject of testimony differed, and for each party the required number of witnesses (niṣāb al-shahāda) was not completed. Quoted from al-'Ināyah. [5] His saying: 'cannot be both voluntary and coerced'—an objection is raised: it is possible that part of it is voluntary and part coerced, so reconciliation is possible and not all witnesses must be lying. The response: consideration is given to the beginning of the act regarding volition and coercion; if it begins as a cause for punishment (ḥadd), it does not revert to not being a cause for punishment, and vice versa.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the effect of witness disagreement on the requirement of consent in zinā testimony. The passage first lists general scenarios where no hadd punishment is applied: witnesses who testify without knowing the woman (because she might be the man's wife or slave), disagreement on consent, location, time, or if the woman is a virgin (or has physical impediments to intercourse), witnesses are immoral, or branch testimony (shahāda 'alā shahāda) is given. In all these cases, neither the accused nor the witnesses are punished. Then the specific dispute is presented: if four witnesses testify, but two say the woman consented (ṭā'i'a) and two say she was coerced (mukraha). According to Abu Hanifa, no hadd is applied to either party. His reasoning: zinā is a single act that cannot simultaneously be voluntary and coerced; therefore, the witnesses contradict each other, and the required number of four witnesses for each version is not met. The Sahibayn hold that the man is punished because all four agree he committed zinā, but the woman is not punished because her consent is disputed. The commentary explains that the Sahibayn view the additional claim of coercion as a separate allegation that does not affect the agreement on the act itself. A further discussion addresses an objection: could the act be partly voluntary and partly coerced? The response is that the ruling is based on the beginning of the act; once the act begins as a cause for hadd (i.e., without consent), it does not change. The relied-upon position in the school is not explicitly given, but the text presents Abu Hanifa's reasoning in detail.

Key Terms
طوع (ṭaw‘): Consent or willingness of the woman to the act of zinā. Contrasted with الإكراه (coercion). In this passage, it is a condition for establishing zinā against the woman.
كره (karh / ikrāh): Coercion; the woman is forced into the act against her will. When established, it exempts the woman from punishment and makes the man solely liable.
شهود على شهود (shuhūd ‘alā shuhūd): Branch testimony; witnesses who testify based on the testimony of original eyewitnesses who are unable to appear. Used as a substitute for direct testimony in zinā cases.
فسقة (fasaqah): Plural of fāsiq, meaning immoral or sinful persons whose testimony is categorically rejected in hadd cases.
حد (ḥadd): Punishment fixed by Allah for specific crimes; in this chapter, the hadd for zinā (lashing or stoning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when four witnesses testify to zinā, but two say the woman consented and two say she was coerced?
A) Both the man and woman are punished with hadd.
B) Only the man is punished with hadd.
C) Only the woman is punished with hadd.
D) Neither the man nor the woman is punished with hadd.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, Abu Hanifa rules that a split on consent in zinā testimony drops the hadd for both, while the Sahibayn punish the man but free the woman.

Dispute on Testimony of Zina When Witnesses Disagree
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness disagreement in zina testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on contradictory witness testimony in zina cases and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from that of the Sahibayn and Zufar.

Core Idea
When four witnesses contradict each other on consent or location, no hadd is imposed on the accused or the witnesses.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of witness disagreement in zina testimony. When four witnesses come forward but differ on the woman's consent or the location of the act, the school's imams diverge. Understanding these nuances clarifies how Hanafi jurists preserve the strict conditions of hadd while avoiding unjust punishment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa: when four witnesses disagree on consent or location, no hadd is applied to the man, woman, or witnesses. Understand his core reasoning: a single act cannot simultaneously have two contradictory descriptions.
This is the baseline position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view (Sahibayn)
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ in the consent-disagreement scenario. They argue that the four witnesses agree on the man's zina, so he should be hadded; the woman is not because her consent is not proven.
The Sahibayn focus on the agreement regarding the man's action.
3
Follow the opponent's proof (Sahibayn and Zufar)
Examine the proofs: Sahibayn rely on the fact that the witnesses all attest to the man committing zina; the disagreement only touches the woman's state. Zufar, in the location dispute, argues that since the testimony is rejected due to insufficient witnesses (each location claim lacks four witnesses), the witnesses should be punished for qadhf.
Zufar's view treats the location disagreement as creating separate claims with incomplete nisab.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds: the act of zina is a single act involving both parties; it cannot be both consensual and coerced. If the witnesses describe contradictory natures, the testimony is defective, and the required number for each specific description is not met. For location, the witnesses all testify to one zina in essence; the location difference creates a shubha that prevents punishing the witnesses.
The response uses the principle of shubha (doubt) to avert hadd.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, no hadd is ever applied in such disagreements. Under the Sahibayn, the man may be hadded if witnesses agree on his action. Under Zufar, the witnesses would be punished for qadhf in location disputes. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's view.
The tarjih is supported by al-Marghinani's commentary (al-Inayah).

[١] قوله: منها؛ الأولى في الموضعين منهم ولعل التأنيث نظراً إلى أن الشهود جمع وهو في حكم التأنيث أو نظراً إلى لفظ أربعة والحاصل: أنه شهد اثنان بأن المرأة كانت طائعة أي راضية بفعله وقال آخران لم تكن طائعة بل أكرهها الرجل. [٤] قوله: لما مر؛ أي لاختلاف المشهود به فإن الفعل يختلف باختلاف المكان فإن كان واحداً فبعضهم كاذب لأن الفعل الواحد لا يوجد في وقت واحد في مكانين وإن لم يكن واحداً فلا نصاب للشهادة على كل منهما. [0] قوله: خلافاً لزفر؛ فإنه يقول بوجوب حد القذف على الشهود في هذه الصورة لأن شهادتهم لما لم تقبل لنقصان العدد صار كلامهم قذفاً. ولنا: إن الأربعة شهدوا مع كونهم أهلاً للشهادة على زنا واحد صورة نظراً إلى اتحاد النسبة الحاصلة منهم واتحاد المرأة وإنما جاء الاختلاف بذكر المكان فتثبت شبهة اتحاد المشهود به ونصاب الشهادة عليه تام ومثل هذه الشبهة تدرؤ عنهم القذف. كذا في «النهاية».
If four witnesses testify, and two of them say she was willing, and two of them say she was coerced, then neither of them (the man and woman) are liable to the hadd penalty according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the man is hadded because the four agreed on his zina, but not the woman due to disagreement [on her consent]. And his proof is: if the act witnessed is one, then some of them are liars, because a single act cannot be both with her willingness and coercion. And if it is not one, then there is no complete number of witnesses for each [act], so they are not hadded. The witnesses are not hadded because the number [of witnesses] is complete. And if four testify to his zina, and they differ on the city of his zina, then neither of them are hadded for the aforementioned reason, nor are the witnesses hadded, contrary to Zufar, because the number is complete.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Wiqayah deals with a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the effect of disagreement among witnesses in a zina case. The ruling is that if four witnesses come forward, but two claim the woman was willing and two claim she was coerced, then Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd is applied to either the man or the woman. His reasoning is that the act of zina is a single act that involves both parties, and a single act cannot simultaneously have two contradictory descriptions (willingness and coercion). Therefore, the witnesses disagree on the essential nature of the act, so the testimony is not legally complete; the required number of four witnesses for each specific assertion is not met. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) differ: they apply the hadd to the man because the four witnesses all agree that he committed zina, though they differ on the woman's state; the man's hadd is established. The woman is not hadded because her consent is a necessary condition for the hadd against her, and this is not proven due to the disagreement. The author then addresses a potential objection: could it be that part of the act was with consent and part by force? The response is that consideration is given to the initial part of the act; if it begins as consensual, it dictates the ruling. The witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation) because the number of witnesses is complete, even if the testimony is not accepted due to the discrepancy. The rule is based on the Quranic verse requiring four witnesses for zina. The passage also covers a second scenario: four witnesses testify but differ on the location of the zina (e.g., two say Basra, two say Damascus). Here, the same reasoning applies: if the act is one, some are lying; if multiple acts, the number of witnesses per act is insufficient. Thus no hadd on the accused, and no hadd on the witnesses. Zufar, however, would impose hadd of qadhf on the witnesses because the testimony is rejected due to insufficient witnesses on each specific claim. The Hanafi answer is that the witnesses were all testifying to one zina in essence (same woman, same accused), and the location difference is a minor discrepancy that creates a doubt (shubha) preventing the qadhf penalty.

Key Terms
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The required number of witnesses for a particular testimony to be legally effective. For zina, the minimum is four witnesses.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment (eighty lashes) for falsely accusing a chaste person of zina, which applies when the accuser fails to produce four witnesses.
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd penalties. In this context, the disagreement among witnesses creates a shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling when four witnesses testify to zina but two say the woman was willing and two say she was coerced?
A) Both the man and woman are hadded.
B) Only the man is hadded.
C) Neither the man nor woman is hadded.
D) Only the witnesses are hadded for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
When four witnesses contradict on consent or location in a zina case, the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) applies no hadd to the accused or the witnesses, based on the principle that a single act cannot have contradictory descriptions and that hadd penalties are averted by doubt.

Contradictory Zina Testimony on Consent: No Hadd
Ruling on zina testimony with internal contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when zina witnesses disagree on consent and explain why no hadd is imposed on the witnesses using Quran 24:4.

Core Idea
Divided testimony on consent fails the four-witness requirement for each act, so no hadd on anyone.

In a zina case, four witnesses came forward but two said the act was consensual and two said it was coerced. How does the Hanafi school rule? This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning: because each version of the act has only two witnesses, the required four are not met for either, so the hadd penalty falls away for both the accused and the witnesses. The proof from the Quran highlights that the punishment for false accusation (qadhf) only applies when fewer than four witnesses are produced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Scenario
Read the passage to understand the specific disagreement: two witnesses say the woman consented, two say she was forced. This creates two separate 'acts' in legal analysis.
2
Apply the Nisaab Requirement
For zina testimony, four witnesses are required to establish a single act. Here each act has only two witnesses, so neither act is proven. Consequently, no hadd (hudud penalty) applies to the accused (the man or the woman).
The hadd is for zina itself; without four witnesses for the same act, the penalty is not imposed.
3
Analyze the Witnesses' Liability
Even though the testimony is not accepted, the witnesses themselves are not punished for qadhf (false accusation). Why? Because four witnesses were produced, fulfilling the literal requirement of Quran 24:4. The verse imposes the qadhf hadd only when 'they do not bring four witnesses.' Since four were brought, the condition is not triggered.
The contradiction makes the testimony unacceptable, but the number requirement is met.
4
Evaluate the Dalil (Proof)
The passage quotes Quran 24:4. The operative phrase is 'lam ya'tu bi-arba'ati shuhada' (did not bring four witnesses). The Hanafi argument uses the plain meaning (zahir): the existence of four witnesses, even if contradictory, prevents the qadhf hadd on the witnesses.
This is a strict textualist reading; other schools might consider the contradiction as effectively making the testimony absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يكن واحد، فلا نصاب للشهادة على كل منهما، ولا يحد الشُّهود
[0] قوله : فلا نصاب ؛ لأنّ الاثنين شهدا بطوعها، واثنان بكرهها فكانت على كل فعل شهادة اثنين، ونصاب الشهادة في باب الزنى أربعة ، فلم يثبت واحـد مـن الفعلين، فلم يجب الحد لا عليه ولا عليها.
[٢] قوله : ولا يحدّ الشهود؛ أي لا يقام على الشهودِ حد القذف ؛ لأنّ نصاب الشهادة تام، وإن لم تقبل لوجود الاختلاف وحد القذف إنما يجب إذا لم يتم نصاب الشهادة، يدلّ عليه قوله : وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَنَّمَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَنِينَ جلدة (1) النور : من الآية .
And if it is not one, then there is no complete number for testimony on each of them, and the witnesses are not punished. [0] His statement: 'then there is no complete number' because the two testified with her consent and two [testified] with her coercion, so for each act there was testimony of two, and the complete number for testimony in the chapter of zina is four, so not one of the two acts was established, so the hadd penalty is not obligatory upon him nor upon her. [2] His statement: 'and the witnesses are not punished' meaning the hadd penalty for false accusation (qadhf) is not imposed on the witnesses, because the complete number of testimony is complete, even if not accepted due to the existence of disagreement, and the hadd penalty for false accusation is only obligatory when the complete number of testimony is not met. This is indicated by His statement: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses - lash them with eighty lashes' (Surah al-Nur, verse 4).
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning testimony for zina when the witnesses disagree on the nature of the act. The matn states that if the testimony is not unified (i.e., the witnesses do not all agree on the same description), then the required number (nisaab) of four witnesses is not met for each individual act, and consequently no hadd penalty is imposed on the accused man or woman, nor are the witnesses punished for false accusation. The commentary explains the reasoning: two witnesses testified that the act was with her consent, and two testified it was by force. Each act thus has only two witnesses, whereas the nisaab for zina testimony is four. Therefore, neither act is legally established, so the hadd penalty is waived for the accused. As for the witnesses, they are not punished under the hadd of qadhf because the total number of witnesses is four, fulfilling the textual requirement. However, the testimony is not accepted due to internal contradiction. The proof is the Quranic verse (24:4) which prescribes eighty lashes for those who accuse chaste women without producing four witnesses. Since four witnesses were produced, the condition for qadhf is not met.

Key Terms
نصاب الشهادة (nisaab al-shahaadah): The required number of witnesses for a particular case; for zina, it is four male witnesses or equivalent.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment (80 lashes) for falsely accusing a chaste person of zina without producing four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where two witnesses say zina was with consent and two say by force, why are the witnesses not punished for qadhf?
A) Because they did not accuse the woman directly.
B) Because the total number of witnesses is four, fulfilling the nisaab, even though the testimony is not accepted.
C) Because the witnesses were not adults.
D) Because the accused admitted guilt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, contradictory testimony on the nature of zina (consent vs. coercion) prevents the hadd penalty for both the accused and the witnesses, as the four-witness requirement for zina is not fulfilled for any single act, and the literal condition for qadhf (fewer than four witnesses) is not met.

Testimony Disagreement on Location: Hanafi vs. Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness disagreement in zina testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority rejects Zufar's view that witnesses who differ on the place of zina must be punished for qadhf, and identify the role of shubhah in averting the hadd.

Core Idea
Disagreement on place does not break the number of witnesses if the act is unified; shubhah averts qadhf.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where four witnesses agree on the person and act of zina but differ on the city. The majority rules that no hadd is imposed on the witnesses because the number is complete and a doubt (shubhah) of unity protects them. Zufar bin al-Hudhayl disagrees, arguing that the testimony is rejected due to deficiency in number, making the witnesses guilty of qadhf. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to apply the principles of hudud and shubhah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): witnesses are not punished for qadhf when they differ on the city of zina, because the number of witnesses is complete (four) and there is a shubhah about the unity of the act.
2
Identify the opponent and his view
Zufar bin al-Hudhayl holds that the witnesses should receive 80 lashes for qadhf, because their testimony is not accepted due to an implied deficiency in the number of witnesses per location.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar, so this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's reasoning: since the witnesses disagree on the place, the testimony is contradictory and not accepted; therefore, for each city there are only two witnesses, which falls short of the required four, making the witnesses false accusers.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority argues that the four witnesses all testify to one zina (same woman, same act) and the only difference is the location. The unity of the subject preserves the complete number (nisaab). The place discrepancy creates a doubt (shubhah) about the exact act, and such a doubt averts the hadd of qadhf.
Key principle: shubhah (doubt) is a legal basis to avoid hudud penalties.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Zufar's view, the witnesses would be lashed 80 times; under the majority view, they are not punished at all. The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شَهدَ أربعة بزناه ، واختلفوا في بلد زناه ، فلا حد عليهما لما مرّ، ولا على الشُّهُودِ خلافاً لزفر له ؛ لوجود العدد.
[٣] قوله : واختلفوا في بلد زناه ؛ فقال اثنان منهم : زني بالبصرة مثلاً، وقال آخران : زنی بدمشق مثلاً.
[٤] قوله : لما مرّ ؛ أي لاختلافِ المشهود به فإنّ الفعل يختلف باختلاف المكان ، فإن كان واحداً فبعضهم كاذب ؛ لأنّ الفعل الواحد لا يوجد في وقت واحدٍ في مكانين وإن لم يكن واحداً فلا نصاب للشهادة على كل منهما. [0] قوله : خلافاً لزفر ه ، فإنّه يقولُ بوجوب حد القذف على الشهود في هذه الصورة؛ لأن شهادتهم لَمّا لم تقبل لنقصان العدد صار كلامهم قذفاً.
ولنا: إن الأربعة شهدوا مع كونهم أهلاً للشهادة على زنا واحد صورة نظراً إلى اتحاد النسبة الحاصلة منهم، واتحاد المرأة، وإنما جاء الاختلاف بذكر المكان، فتثبت شبهة اتحاد المشهود به ونصاب الشهادة عليه تام، ومثلُ هذه الشبهة تدرؤ عنهم القذف. كذا في «النهاية».
And if four testify to his zina, and they differ regarding the city of his zina, then there is no hadd on them (the accused) due to what has passed, and no [hadd] on the witnesses, contrary to Zufar, because the number is complete. [3] His statement: 'and they differed regarding the city of his zina' – for example, two of them said he committed zina in Basra, and the other two said he committed zina in Damascus. [4] His statement: 'due to what has passed' – meaning due to the difference in the testified act, for the act differs by place. If it is one, then some of them are lying, because one act cannot occur in one time in two places; and if it is not one, then there is no complete number for testimony on each of them. [0] His statement: 'contrary to Zufar' – for he says that the hadd of qadhf is obligatory on the witnesses in this scenario, because since their testimony is not accepted due to deficiency in number, their words become qadhf. 
Our [Hanafi] argument: The four testified while being qualified to testify concerning one zina in form, considering the unity of the attribution from them, and the unity of the woman, and the difference only came by mentioning the place, so a doubt (shubhah) of the unity of the testified act is established, and the complete number of testimony upon it is complete, and such a doubt averts from them the qadhf. This is stated in al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Zufar bin al-Hudhayl. The matn rules that when four witnesses agree on the person but differ on the city of zina, no hadd is imposed on the accused (because the testimony is contradictory) and no hadd is imposed on the witnesses (because the number of witnesses is complete). Zufar disagrees: he argues that since the testimony is not accepted due to an implied deficiency in number (because the disagreement suggests that for each place there are only two witnesses), the witnesses should be punished for qadhf. The Hanafi majority responds by emphasizing that the four witnesses all testified to a single act of zina from the same woman, and the only difference is the location. This creates a doubt (shubhah) about the unity of the act. The complete number of witnesses (four) is present, and such a doubt is sufficient to avert the hadd of qadhf. The authority cited is al-Nihayah (likely a reference). The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or ambiguity that can avert a hadd penalty. Here, the possibility that the act is one and the location error is incidental.
عدد (adad): Number; here refers to the required number of witnesses (four) for zina testimony.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; punishable by 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi majority not punish witnesses who differ on the city of zina?
A) Because the witnesses are all credible and did not intentionally lie.
B) Because the number of witnesses is complete (four) and a doubt (shubhah) about the unity of the act averts qadhf.
C) Because the accused is not punished, so the witnesses cannot be punished.
D) Because the witnesses later agreed on the city.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses agree on the person and act of zina but differ on the place, the Hanafi majority protects them from qadhf due to the complete number and the doubt (shubhah) of unity, a principle that prioritizes the integrity of the testimony over minor discrepancies.

Contradictory Testimony in Zina: No Hadd Due to Doubt
Ruling on contradictory testimony in zina with impossibility of concurrence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when two contradictory testimonies create certainty of falsehood without specific identification, no hadd is imposed on the accused or the witnesses, and explain the role of doubt (shubhah) in averting the hadd.

Core Idea
Certain falsehood without identification shields both accused and witnesses from hadd.

This lesson examines a unique scenario where two groups of four witnesses each testify that the accused committed zina at the exact same moment, but in different cities. By rational necessity, one group must be lying. The Hanafi school teaches that this certainty of falsehood without identification leads to rejection of all testimony, and the possibility of truthfulness for each group individually creates a doubt that averts the hadd of qadhf from the witnesses. We will unpack the legal reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Two groups of four witnesses each testify that the accused committed zina at the same specific time but in two different cities.
This physical impossibility is the crux of the case.
2
Recognize the logical impossibility
One person cannot be in two places at once, so one group must be lying. This yields certainty of falsehood (tayaqqun al-kadhib) for one group, but we do not know which.
3
Apply the rule of contradictory testimony
Since there is no preponderance (rajah) for either group, both testimonies are rejected. The accused are not punished because zina is not proven.
The hadd on the accused is averted due to lack of clear proof.
4
Apply the rule of doubt (shubhah) for the witnesses
Even though one group is certainly lying, each group individually could be truthful (the falsehood is unspecified). This possibility of truth creates a doubt that prevents the hadd of qadhf from being imposed on any witness.
The hadd of qadhf requires certainty that the accusation is false; here, falsehood is not certain for any given group.
5
Distinguish the case where one group lacks conditions
If one group does not meet the conditions for testimony (e.g., integrity) and the other does, the qualified group's testimony is accepted and the other is rejected, altering the ruling.
This exception highlights the importance of witness qualifications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شَهِدَ أربعة بزناه في وقت معين) ، وأربعة أخرى بزناه في ذلك الوقت في بلد آخر، فلا حد عليهما ؛ لأنَّ شهادة أحد الفريقين مردودة ؛ لتيقن كذبه ، ولا رجحان" لأحدهما فيرد الجميع ، ولا على الشهود ؛ لاحتمال صدق أحد الفريقين"
[1] قوله : فلا حد عليهما ؛ أي على الرجل والمرأة ؛ لأنّ كذب أحد الفريقين متيقن لعدم إمكان صدور فعل واحدٍ من رجل واحد في وقت واحد في مكانين متباعدين ، فلم يثبت الزني بشهادة أحدهما.
[٢] قوله : ولا رجحان ؛ يعني ليس في أحد الفريقين ما يُرجح قبوله على الآخر، وفيه احتراز عما لو لم توجد في أحد الفريقين شرائط قبول الشهادة، ووجدت في الآخر، فحينئذ تقبل شهادة الفريق المجتمعة لصفات القبول وتردّ شهادة الآخر.
[3] قوله : لاحتمال صدق أحد الفريقين ; الأولى أن يقول : لاحتمال صدق كلّ من الفريقين، كما في «الهداية».
والحاصل : إن صدق كلّ من الفريقين محتمل ، وكذب أحدهما لا بعينه متيقن ، فلتيقن كذب أحدهما دُرِءَ الحد عن الرَّجل والمرأة، ولاحتمال صدق كلِّ منهما دُرِءَ الحد عن الشهود الثمانية ; لأنَّ حد القذف إنّما يقام إذا لم يثبت الزنا ولم توجد شبهة ، وهاهنا شبهة الزنا قائمة لاحتمال صدق الشهود.
فإن قلت : كيف يجتمع احتمال صدق كل منهما مع تيقن كذب أحدهما، بل لا يكون هاهنا إلا احتمال صدق أحدهما.
قلت : تيقن الكذب متعلق بأحدهما لا بعينه، وهو لا يضر في وجود احتمال الصدق في كل منهما على انفراده، وإنّ ما يضر احتمال صدق مجموعهما. ويمكن أن يقال : إن صدق كل منهما وإن كان محتملاً ، لكن وجود احتمال الصدق في أحدهما لا بعينه أيضاً كافٍ لدرء الحدّ عن الشهود، فلذلك اكتفى عليه الشارح ، فافهم هذا فإنّه مع أكثر ما مرّ وما يأتي في هذا البحث من سوانح الوقت.
And if four testify to his zina at a specific time, and another four [testify] to his zina at that same time in another city, then there is no hadd on them (the accused) because the testimony of one of the two groups is rejected due to the certainty of its falsehood, and there is no preponderance for one over the other, so all are rejected; and no [hadd] on the witnesses due to the possibility of truthfulness of one of the two groups. [1] His statement: 'then no hadd on them' – meaning on the man and woman, because the falsehood of one of the two groups is certain due to the impossibility of a single act from one man at one time in two distant places, so zina is not established by the testimony of either. [2] His statement: 'and no preponderance' – meaning there is nothing in one of the two groups that would make it preferable for acceptance over the other, and this excludes the case where one group lacks the conditions for acceptance of testimony and the other possesses them; in that case, the testimony of the group possessing the qualities of acceptance is accepted and the other is rejected. [3] His statement: 'due to the possibility of truthfulness of one of the two groups' – the better expression is 'due to the possibility of truthfulness of each of the two groups', as in al-Hidayah.
The conclusion: The truthfulness of each group is possible, and the falsehood of one of them (not specifically identified) is certain. Due to the certainty of falsehood of one, the hadd is averted from the man and woman; and due to the possibility of truthfulness of each, the hadd is averted from the eight witnesses, because the hadd of qadhf is only imposed when zina is not established and no doubt (shubhah) exists; and here the doubt of zina exists due to the possibility of truthfulness of the witnesses.
If you say: How can the possibility of truthfulness of each coexist with the certainty of falsehood of one? Rather, here there is only possibility of truthfulness of one of them. 
I say: Certainty of falsehood is attached to one of them not specifically, and that does not harm the existence of possibility of truthfulness in each individually; rather, what would harm is the possibility of truthfulness of both collectively. It can also be said: Even if the truthfulness of each is possible, the existence of the possibility of truthfulness in one of them (not specifically) is sufficient to avert the hadd from the witnesses, therefore the commentator sufficed with that. Understand this, for it is along with most of what has passed and what will come in this research of the flashes of the time.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling involving two groups of four witnesses each, all testifying that the accused committed zina at the same specific time but in two different cities. Since it is physically impossible for one person to be in two places at once, one group must be lying, but there is no way to determine which. Therefore, the testimony of both groups is rejected, and no hadd is imposed on the accused man and woman. The reasoning is that the falsehood of one group is certain, so the zina is not proven. As for the eight witnesses, they are not punished for qadhf because each group has the possibility of being truthful (i.e., it is possible that they are not lying, even though we know one group is lying, we don't know which). This possibility creates a doubt (shubhah) that averts the hadd. The commentary further refines the expression: it is better to say 'possibility of truthfulness of each group' rather than 'one group', because the doubt exists for each individual group considered separately. The analysis emphasizes that the certainty of falsehood applies to one group without identification, which does not preclude the possibility of truthfulness of each individually. Therefore, the hadd of qadhf is not imposed.

Key Terms
تيقن الكذب (tayaqqun al-kadhib): Certainty of falsehood – here, it is logically certain that one of the two groups is lying because the events cannot coincide.
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt that prevents the application of a hadd penalty – in this case, the possibility that each group is truthful creates a shubhah that averts the hadd of qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the eight witnesses not punished for qadhf in the case of two groups testifying to zina at the same time in different places?
A) Because the accused were not convicted.
B) Because the number of witnesses per group is less than four.
C) Because there is a possibility of truthfulness for each group, creating a doubt that averts the hadd.
D) Because the witnesses recanted their testimony.

Key Takeaway
When certainty of falsehood is not specific to a particular witness or group, the possibility of truth for each creates a doubt that prevents the hadd of qadhf.
